Narrative Grid

      Personal Context
      
        
          
            üß© Part 1 ‚Äî Narrative Structure of Fact
          

          
            Function: This part opens the
            narrative grid, a three-part structure designed to document
            ‚Äî rather than interpret ‚Äî key stages of a workplace conflict. It
            lays out how, when, and under what intent I entered the situation.
          

          
            Fields: This kind of structure appears as a
            case chronology
            (legal), a
            mission log (ops), or an
            incident report (HR).
            Comparable formats exist in investigative journalism, field
            diagnostics, and strategic consulting.
          

          
            Usage: Lawyers, auditors, and compliance agents use
            such forms to detect
            managerial drift,
            accountability gaps,
            or signs of
            proxy communication
            in hierarchical systems.
          

          
            Adaptation: This structure is here deployed as a
            preemptive layer ‚Äî not to persuade, but to resist. It
            anticipates legal tactics aiming to minimize damage by framing the
            claimant as incoherent, fragile, or unserious.
          

          
            Structure: The narrative follows a strict
            3-paragraph model: intent, chronology, and strategic framing. It
            presents no claim and no emotion ‚Äî only a foundation.
          

          
            üìö Continue the grid:
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/working-dynamics.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 2 ‚Äì Process Narative</a
            >
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/governance.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 3 ‚Äì Authority Mapping</a
            >
          
        
      

      Working Dynamics

      
        
          
            üîÑ Part 2 ‚Äî Process Narrative
          

          
            Function: To reconstruct how work actually unfolded
            ‚Äî who gave instructions, who took charge, and how roles shifted
            beyond official titles or contracts.
          

          
            Fields: Known as a
            process narrative
            (HR),
            <a href="/glossary.html#functional-ethnography"
              >functional ethnography</a
            >
            (sociology), or
            workflow mapping
            (audit). All describe how systems operate below the surface.
          

          
            Usage: Used by compliance officers, workplace
            mediators, and researchers to clarify informal routines, relational
            tensions, and decision patterns that don‚Äôt appear in formal
            hierarchies.
          

          
            Adaptation: This section captures how fragmented
            authority and social silences shaped daily life. It tracks where
            guidance came from, who avoided responsibility, and how staff
            compensated through informal channels.
          

          
            Structure: The narrative follows a chronological
            logic, grounded in first-person memory and interaction flow. It
            prioritizes lived routines over documentation.
          

          
            üìö Explore the full grid:
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/context.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 1 ‚Äì Narrative Structure of Fact</a
            >
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/governance.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 3 ‚Äì Authority Mapping</a
            >
          
        
      

      Operational Authority
      
        
          
            üï∏Ô∏è Part 3 ‚Äî Authority Mapping
          

          
            Function: To trace how decisions were made,
            delegated, or avoided ‚Äî and how visible and invisible roles shaped
            the workplace structure.
          

          
            Fields: This method appears in
            authority mapping
            (audit),
            governance reviews,
            and
            decision tracing in
            management and legal investigations.
          

          
            Usage: These tools are used to detect
            proxy authority,
            responsibility gaps, and
            unspoken hierarchies ‚Äî especially where formal
            titles mask operational control.
          

          
            Adaptation: This section identifies
            social roles, silences,
            disconnections, and improvisation.
            It exposes how instructions circulated without structure, and how
            power was enacted informally.
          

          
            Structure: The narrative isolates key moments of
            implied authority. It focuses on contrasts ‚Äî between who was legally
            in charge, and who shaped the team‚Äôs behavior in practice.
          

          
            üìö Explore the full grid:
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/context.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 1 ‚Äì Narrative Structure of Fact</a
            >
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/working-dynamics.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 2 ‚Äì Process Narrative</a
            >

          How to read this section
        

        
          This is the third entry in a triptych exploring the practical,
          interpersonal, and structural conditions of a workplace conflict. It
          complements Context and
          Working Dynamics
        

        
          This final part focuses on
          <strong
            >role expectations, managerial presence, and internal authority
            patterns</strong
          >
          ‚Äî especially when formal contracts fail to reflect operational
          reality.
        

        
          In corporate sociology or organizational diagnostics, this type of
          narrative aligns with a role-mapping audit or a
          governance ambiguity assessment.
        

        
          It helps clarify not only who was meant to lead, but
          also who actually did ‚Äî and where the gaps, silences,
          or reversals emerged.

AfterShift Blog

      
        This space will soon host a series of written chronicles, drawing from
        my lived experience in Malm√∂'s restaurant industry.
      
      
        Each article will explore two dimensions: the chronological unfolding of
        events, and a parallel legal reflection based on those facts.
      

      
        First upcoming post: On dismissal by text ‚Äî a
        reflection on the normalization of termination without explanation or
        documentation.
      

      
        Before launching the first entries, legal disclaimers and policy details
        are being finalized.

      Legal Notice &amp; Data Policy

      1. Site Publisher
      
        Site owner: Patrice Kenmo√© (individual)
        Address: Hyllie Boulevard 34, 215 32 Malm√∂, Sweden
        Email: patrice@aftershift.se
      

      2. Hosting
      
        Hosted by GitHub, Inc.
        88 Colin P. Kelly Jr Street, San Francisco, CA 94107, USA
      

      3. Purpose of the Blog
      
        AfterShift is a personal blog documenting legal reflections and lived
        experience in the context of labor, legal inertia, and social structure.
        It is neither a company nor a journalistic entity. Its tone is personal,
        reflective, and evolving.
      

      4. Legal Status
      
        The blog is managed by an individual based in Sweden and follows Swedish
        legal jurisdiction. Any disputes shall be handled by the courts of
        Malm√∂.
      

      5. Editorial Responsibility
      
        The blog is authored by Patrice Kenmo√©. All content is self-published.
        Names and details may be anonymized to ensure privacy and legal safety.
      

      6. Disclaimer
      
        
          This blog represents personal experience and analysis. It is not
          intended to target individuals or damage reputations. The aim is to
          document systemic issues and provide structured, respectful
          commentary. Content is subject to frequent updates as the platform
          evolves.
        

        
          In narrative sections of the blog, certain personal names may be
          altered to protect the identity of individuals. These changes are made
          in good faith and aim to balance narrative clarity with respect for
          privacy. Any resemblance to real persons, living or dead, outside of
          documented facts, is coincidental.
        
      

      7. Commenting &amp; Feedback
      
        
          The AfterShift blog includes a comment system (currently planned via
          Giscus, a lightweight tool built on GitHub Discussions).
        
        
          Giscus requires a GitHub account to participate in discussions. This
          choice was made for fast deployment and is not intended to restrict
          participation.
        
        
          Users who cannot or do not wish to use GitHub may contact us via email
          or participate through other platforms (e.g., OB1 Circles).
        
        
          As the platform evolves, comments may migrate to alternative tools
          (e.g., Commento or embedded forms), provided privacy and legal
          compliance are maintained.
        
        
          All significant changes will be clearly communicated via updated terms
          or page footers.
        
      

      8. Intellectual Property
      
        All texts, visuals, and documents are original creations and property of
        Patrice Kenmo√© unless otherwise stated. No reproduction is permitted
        without written consent.
      

      9. Privacy &amp; Data
      
        No personal data is collected without consent. Matomo Analytics may be
        used in full compliance with GDPR regulations. No cookies or identifiers
        are used to track individuals.
      

      10. Evolution &amp; Versioning
      
        This blog is updated daily and may evolve significantly over time. Legal
        notices and key policy documents are versioned and may change regularly.
        Changes will be documented and dated.
      

      11. Cross-site Relationship
      
        AfterShift is independent but connected to OB1.se (a separate community
        platform). Both are maintained by the same author but serve different
        purposes. Legal responsibilities are clearly separated.

      Press & Legal Access

      
        This page provides structured access for journalists, legal advisors, or
        labor advocates who wish to engage with AfterShift's content. Whether
        your goal is to reference, clarify, or challenge specific information,
        this guide outlines available channels and responsibilities.
      

      üéôÔ∏è For Journalists
      
        
          All content is original and publicly accessible under Swedish
          editorial protection.
        
        
          Reproductions are permitted with citation:
          ‚ÄúAfterShift.se‚Äù and date of access.
        
        
          Interview requests, background questions, or fact-checks can be
          submitted via the contact form or email:
          patrice@aftershift.se
        
      

      ‚öñÔ∏è For Legal Professionals
      
        
          The blog documents lived experience, factual records, and formal
          documents (contracts, payslips, HRAK letters).
        
        
          If you represent a party mentioned, or a regulatory body, please
          include reference dates or filenames in your message.
        
        
          Requests for correction or legal rebuttal are acknowledged under
          Swedish law (see Defense FAQ).
        
        No hidden tracking or paywall restricts access to evidence.
      

      üß∞ Legal & Editorial Framing
      
        
          The project is documented under civic journalism and editorial
          responsibility.
        
        
          Names and companies are mentioned when directly tied to structural
          facts or proven misconduct.
        
        
          Any redacted content or aliases are used to protect personal privacy
          or pending investigations.
        
      

      ü§ù Collaboration & Verification
      
        Contributions or suggestions are welcome from:
        
          Labor law experts
          Investigative reporters
          Union officials or ombudsm√§n
          Academic researchers
        
        All contributions are attributed unless otherwise agreed.
      

      
        This page reflects the editorial transparency policy of AfterShift.
        Questions may be addressed to the site author.

            On Dismissal by SMS
            
              Published: May 3, 2025
              Event date: December 14, 2024
              Last updated: May 6, 2025
              Type of article: Structured factual report
              Tags: labor law, restaurant, Sweden, SMS
    

    
      Structural Format: Circumstantial Exposition Model
    
      
        This article adopts what is commonly referred to as a Circumstantial Exposition Model: a hybrid structure designed to document real-life incidents with both narrative clarity and legal coherence.
      
    
      
        It combines chronological narration, factual anchoring, and interpretive layers to support legal, journalistic, or institutional assessments.
        
        In legal writing, this structure appears as a case brief or factual memorandum. 
        
        In investigative journalism, it is reflected in timeline-driven expos√©s.
        
       In academic research, the format resembles case-centered reflections.
        
        In HR or compliance contexts, it parallels whistleblower reports.
    
      
        The core objective is to track events as they unfold, qualify breaches, and assess consequences ‚Äî without fictionalising or speculating. It supports both evidentiary scrutiny and systemic analysis.
      

      
        This model combines chronological narration and factual anchoring with interpretive layers ‚Äî offering a method suited for documenting workplace disputes or legal infractions without dramatization.
      
      
      
        In this article, the chosen perspective is first-person: all facts are narrated by the individual directly affected, and grounded in verifiable documentation. This supports both legal coherence and narrative legitimacy.
      
    

    
      Article Structure (5-step internal guide)
    
      
        Contextual background ‚Äì where, when, under what conditions
        Chronological unfolding ‚Äì facts laid out with timestamps
        Qualification of the breach ‚Äì what makes it problematic or unlawful
        Reactions and consequences ‚Äì both immediate and downstream
        Comparative societal reflection ‚Äì contrasting legal expectations in Sweden vs. the US
      
    
    
      At 6:35 AM on December 14, 2024, after a work shift that ended slightly earlier than usual, I sent a message to management proposing to take a short break. The message included an additional note: if the proposal was not accepted, they could interpret the text as a resignation.
      
      
      
      Several hours later, a manager acknowledged receipt and said the matter would be discussed. No follow-up occurred during the day.
      
      
      
      On the following day, December 15, at 11:30 AM, I was notified by SMS that the management had decided to ‚Äúpart ways.‚Äù This article reconstructs the events, documents the exchanges, and examines the legal and procedural implications of the termination.
      

      
        Disclaimer: For confidentiality purposes, certain names (e.g., ‚ÄúMina‚Äù, ‚ÄúErik‚Äù) have been altered. The chronology and content remain accurate and based on verifiable events.
      
          
            
            Screenshot of the actual dismissal SMS (names blurred)
          
          
            In December 2024, I was employed as a dishwasher at Quan, a restaurant located inside the Elite Hotel Esplanade in Malm√∂. Although I had no written contract, I worked regular late-night shifts, typically finishing between 4:30 and 5:30 AM, with occasional earlier or longer closings.
            
            
            
            I had no direct contact with the hotel‚Äôs administration. My only supervisor was a woman named Mina, who acted as manager on-site. She gave instructions, managed schedules, and appeared to oversee daily operations, though her exact formal title or role within the company was never disclosed.
              
            
             
                
                  From November 23 to December 15, 2024, I worked as a dishwasher in a restaurant located inside a luxury hotel in Malm√∂, known for being fully booked several weeks in advance. The onboarding was informal: no written contract, no introduction to rules or expectations, and no outline of duties. The work relied on informal verbal cues and implicit norms.
                
              
                
                  There was no team-wide communication channel, aside from the shared schedule system (Personalkollen). Instructions came mainly from Emil, a manager operating mostly via SMS. Floor-level authority, however, seemed to rest with Mina, whose role was never explicitly defined, yet who visibly directed staff on site. I was never formally introduced to her or briefed on her function.
                
              
                
                  On December 14, I made several verbal attempts to clarify my role, especially regarding a test period where I was unofficially expected to replace the external cleaning team. Over the span of a few hours, I addressed Mina multiple times, asking for a short exchange. My requests were either ignored, deflected ("go speak to Magnus"), or met with ironic laughter.
                
              
                
                  In one instance, she walked away laughing with a colleague after I asked a basic question. Another time, she responded with a dismissive look. Only once‚Äîwhen noticing my visible disappointment‚Äîdid she give a brief answer in front of another staff member. By the end of the shift, I was physically strained from repeated hand injuries and carrying a significant sleep debt, and mentally affected by the persistent lack of recognition and clarity.
                
                
                  That evening, I attempted several times to speak with Mina, seeking clarity on my duties ‚Äî especially regarding the trial replacement of the external Friday cleaning service. She reminded me I was still on a trial period and said it wasn‚Äôt the right time. I acknowledged this and backed off initially.
                
                
                
                  Later, when the environment seemed calmer, I tried again. I had become more familiar with the team and the place, and I felt increasingly confident initiating that kind of exchange. But she either avoided me, dismissed the request, or responded with sarcasm. One interaction even ended with a smirk and her walking away mid-sentence.
                
                
                
                  Despite these attempts, Mina had earlier encouraged me to take on extra duties, and the head chef had said he might make me the ‚Äúmain guy.‚Äù Still, I received no clear instructions. Erik, the other manager visible in media, remained silent. He never introduced himself formally nor spoke about work. The two managers seemed to operate independently and barely acknowledged each other. I found myself isolated and uncertain who to approach.

Perspectives and Ideas
      <small class="timestamp" style="display: block; text-align: center"
        >Last updated: Thursday, May 1, 2025 at 02:20 AM</small
      >

      
        This blog is currently in its early development stage. While not
        intended for full-scale content publication yet, it serves as a
        structural prototype to define the foundations of a more comprehensive
        and SEO-oriented platform. Only minimal publication activity is planned
        during this phase. Updates focus on setting up the framework,
        structuring content, and ensuring traceability through a documented log.
        This documentation approach aligns with key principles of transparency,
        traceability, and good faith. Those interested in understanding the
        broader context are invited to explore the rationale behind this log.

      Reading Help

      
        This section is designed to help readers understand the structure and logic behind the AfterShift archive.
        It is not a blog in the conventional sense ‚Äî it is a layered civic testimony built with legal and editorial intention.
      

      üß≠ What this archive contains
      
        Chronological posts documenting events and grievances as they unfolded
        Fact-based reconstructions of employment abuse, contract denial, wage theft
        Structural analyses of corporate opacity and hidden employer responsibility
        Legal framing tools such as glossary, FAQ, or timeline
        Public evidence (e.g. payslips, certificates, email captures)
      

      üìö How to navigate
      
        Start with Personal Context and Editorial Framework
        Use the Timeline for event-based navigation
        Consult the Glossary if legal or technical terms are unclear
        Refer to Defense FAQ for legal boundaries and intent
        Visit Notes for deep dives into corporate or procedural anomalies
      

      üß† What to keep in mind
      
        This is a real situation, involving real legal and financial damage
        The tone is factual, deliberate, and non-emotional ‚Äî even when the content is serious
        The site is not intended as a diary but as a reference dossier for legal, journalistic, or civic use
        Each post is linked to one or more verifiable documents
      

      üí¨ Questions or clarifications?
      
        If something is unclear, or if you'd like to contribute, correct, or discuss a specific post, feel free to:
        
          Use the contact form
          Email: patrice@aftershift.se
        
        I welcome all respectful inquiries ‚Äî whether legal, journalistic, or personal.

      Profil
      
        
          My name is Patrice Kenmo√©, I‚Äôm 47 years old. Born in
          Lyon, of Bamil√©k√© ethnicity, I‚Äôve
          lived in six countries. After three years in Ireland, I moved to
          Sweden on April 21st, 2022.
        

        
          At 25, I left France for the first time: destination
          the Netherlands, where I worked in several call
          centers. Back in France, I returned to sales, then discovered the job
          of hotliner, my first real gateway into IT.
        

        
          At 29, I started an IT training course, and before
          finishing it, I was recruited by HP in Barcelona,
          then IBM in Amsterdam. I spent
          two and a half years abroad, before returning to
          France at 32, where I worked as a consultant at
          Sanofi.
        

        
          At 35, in conflict with my values, I walked away from
          everything. I left the highest-paying job I‚Äôd ever had to move to
          Berlin.
        

        
          Between 35 and 45, I worked barely a year in total. I
          sometimes lived without stable housing, sometimes in
          emergency shelters, sometimes
          in rentals or with a partner. It was a time of
          rupture, of deep questioning, when I began to shape
          my own principles of life.
        

        
          At 45, I moved to Sweden. I spent nearly a year in Gothenburg, then
          about 15 months in Stockholm, much of it in a relationship. For the
          past 6 months, I‚Äôve been living in Malm√∂, where a
          new chapter has quietly started.
        
        
          ‚öñÔ∏è This biography reflects the author's personal experience and legal
          observations. It does not constitute legal advice or institutional
          reporting. Some names and identifiers may be modified to preserve
          privacy and focus on structural critique.

      Operational Authority
  
        
          This part completes the narrative grid ‚Äî by focusing on how
          authority was distributed, claimed, or blurred throughout the
          workplace conflict.
        
        
          
            üï∏Ô∏è Part 3 ‚Äî Authority Mapping
          

          
            Function: To trace how decisions were made,
            delegated, or avoided ‚Äî and how visible and invisible roles shaped
            the workplace structure.
          

          
            Fields: This method appears in
            authority mapping
            (audit),
            governance reviews,
            and
            decision tracing in
            management and legal investigations.
          

          
            Usage: These tools are used to detect
            proxy authority,
            responsibility gaps, and
            unspoken hierarchies ‚Äî especially where formal
            titles mask operational control.
          

          
            Adaptation: This section identifies
            social roles, silences,
            disconnections, and improvisation.
            It exposes how instructions circulated without structure, and how
            power was enacted informally.
          

          
            Structure: The narrative isolates key moments of
            implied authority. It focuses on contrasts ‚Äî between who was legally
            in charge, and who shaped the team‚Äôs behavior in practice.
          

          
            üìö Explore the full grid:
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/context.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 1 ‚Äì Narrative Structure of Fact</a
            >
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/working-dynamics.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 2 ‚Äì Process Narrative</a
            >
          
        
      

      
        The ambiguity in responsibility at the heart of Quan‚Äôs management ‚Äî
        marked by avoidance, blurred roles,
        and a lack of steady accountability ‚Äî struck me the
        most. It naturally led to an archaeology of how this scaffolding was
        laid.
      

      
        When I first considered applying at Quan, I conducted a standard
        ownership check to tailor my motivation email.
        <strong
          >Henrik Kei Siebert was the only visible public figure linked to the
          restaurant</strong
        >, repeatedly cited in hotel communications and online articles as its
        founder.
      

      
        <strong
          >No trace of a distinct legal entity operating Quan appeared in public
          records</strong
        >, which left me uncertain about whom to address‚Äîand forced me to send a
        generic, unpersonalized message.
      

      
        My job interview had been conducted by a woman who introduced herself as
        Sahar‚Äî"like Sahara", she said. Only later, by
        cross-checking the name in Personalkollen, did I understand she held a
        formal role within HSSC Event AB.
      

      
        Despite this, Henrik Kei Siebert‚Äîthe only visible
        public figure associated with Quan‚Äîdid not appear anywhere in official
        records. His absence from the company‚Äôs registration was surprising,
        given his public role and occasional presence on site.
      

      
        According to the Swedish Beneficial Ownership Register,
        HSSC Event AB is controlled by KEHDA Holding AB, through which Lin
        Daniella Dahl holds between 50‚Äì75% of the shares. Her name is absent
        from operational documents and restaurant-facing materials.
      

      
        The domain quanbyquan.se, which has hosted Quan‚Äôs
        website since 2018, was registered on 24 August 2018.
        WHOIS data discloses no owner identity, and the site contains no
        impressum or corporate details.
      

      
        Throughout my three weeks of employment at Quan,
        Saahil Chudasama‚Äîofficially listed as a co-owner‚Äîwas
        never seen on-site. No colleague ever mentioned him,
        and his name played no role in daily operations.
      


        (2018‚Äì2024) confirm none of these elements ever appeared on the site.
      

      
        Henrik‚Äôs role appeared
        detached from the daily team flow. I never witnessed
        him share a joke, give a directive, or interact casually with staff.
        From my position in the back kitchen, he always seemed removed, even
        when physically present.
      
      
        By contrast,
        Sahar was visibly active in team coordination. I saw
        her engage directly with the floor manager, the head chef, and multiple
        sous-chefs‚Äîoften inside the kitchen. She also managed interviews and
        subcontractor issues. There was no doubt she operated at the core of
        daily operations.
      

      <details
      open
      style="
        background-color: #e5e7eb;
        border-radius: 0.6rem;
        padding: 1.5rem;
        margin: 1.5rem 0;
        line-height: 1.6;
      "
    >
      
        üìå Structural Note: Informal Leadership, Formal Incorporation
      
      

      No internal communication or shared leadership structure was visible
      during the observed period. Staff routines followed
      practical rather than hierarchical logic, with no
      direct managerial access linked to the
      two registered owners.

      This model coexisted with
      remarkable financial output‚Äîreportedly over 5 million
      SEK in net profit in 2023, and
      3 weeks of advance booking at all times. The later
      registration of Tributum AB may indicate a step toward
      structural consolidation or structural clarity.
    


    
      Tributum AB officially declared a business activity of
      restaurant operations (restaurangverksamhet). Its board
      includes Henrik Kei Siebert as CEO,
      Sahar El Nasser as board member, and
      Lin Daniella Dahl as deputy. This configuration mirrors
      operational roles already observed at Quan.
    

    
      This synchronised registration raises strategic questions. While
      Tributum AB was presented as a formal clarification of
      restaurant activity, Aspiratio could serve as a
      holding or fallback structure, or as a shielded platform
      disconnected from declared payroll operations.
    

    <details
    open
    style="
      background-color: #e5e7eb;
      border-radius: 0.6rem;
      padding: 1.5rem;
      margin: 1.5rem 0;
      line-height: 1.6;
    "
  >
    
      üìå Structural Insight: Dual Entities, Silent Repositioning
    

    
      The mirrored setup of Tributum AB and
      Aspiratio Holding AB, both created on July 1st at the
      same address, goes beyond administrative convenience.
      Their design suggests an attempt to
      redistribute roles,
      separate exposures, and
      clarify legal responsibility.
    

    
      While Tributum declared active restaurant operations,
      Aspiratio remains structurally dormant: no payroll,
      no declared business. This silent setup may offer
      future flexibility,
      discreet compensation flows, or
      risk management beyond the main operation.
    
    
      This dual setup could act as a buffer‚Äîabsorbing
      pressure, shielding liability, or preparing for change‚Äîwithout public
      disclosure or fiscal trace.
    

    
      Despite being officially registered only as a
      suppleant (alternate board member), her signature confirms an
      operational role in human resources. It also implies
      her position as the primary interface with
      external entities such as HRAK.
    

    
      Separately, the employment certificate issued in my
      name was signed by Sahar El Nasser. This formal act
      establishes her involvement in administrative and personnel matters,
      beyond her nominal board position.

        This section will soon feature a handful of articles. Each release will

        stage‚Äîsix articles maximum. The objective is to explore
        formats, refine editorial tone, and prepare for a future advanced
        platform.

      Working Dynamics

      
        
          This part continues the narrative grid ‚Äî a pragmatic label
          for a three-part structure used to examine how a conflict was shaped
          through its early framing, internal operations, and implicit power
          dynamics.
        

        
          
            üîÑ Part 2 ‚Äî Process Narrative
          

          
            Function: This section reconstructs how work
            actually unfolded ‚Äî who gave instructions, who took charge, and how
            roles shifted beyond official titles or contracts.
          

          
            Fields: Known as a
            process narrative (HR),
            functional ethnography (sociology), or
            workflow mapping (audit). All describe how systems
            operate below the surface.
          

          
            Usage: Used by compliance officers, workplace
            mediators, and researchers to clarify informal routines, relational
            tensions, and decision patterns that don‚Äôt appear in formal
            hierarchies.
          

          
            Adaptation: This section captures how fragmented
            authority and social silences shaped daily life. It tracks where
            guidance came from, who avoided responsibility, and how staff
            compensated through informal channels.
          

          
            Structure: The narrative follows a chronological
            logic, grounded in first-person memory and interaction flow. It
            prioritizes lived routines over documentation.
          

          
            üìö Explore the full grid:
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/context.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 1 ‚Äì Narrative Structure of Fact</a
            >
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/governance.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 3 ‚Äì Authority Mapping</a
            >
          
        
      
      

      
        Quan operates physically within the premises of Elite Hotel Esplanade,
        at M√§ster Johansgatan 15 in Malm√∂. While customers often believe they
        are dealing directly with hotel staff,
        <strong
          >the restaurant is managed independently, under separate legal
          entities</strong
        >.
      

      
        The integration is logistical rather than visual: Quan
        shares the physical space of the hotel, but
        <strong
          >employment and managerial responsibilities are externalized to
          private companies</strong
        >
        with no direct affiliation to the Elite Hotels group.
      

      
        When I first considered applying at Quan, I conducted a standard
        ownership check to tailor my motivation email.
        <strong
          >Henrik Kei Siebert was the only visible public figure linked to the
          restaurant</strong
        >, repeatedly cited in hotel communications and online articles as its
        founder.
      

      
        <strong
          >No trace of a distinct legal entity operating Quan appeared in public
          records</strong
        >, which left me uncertain about whom to address‚Äîand forced me to send a
        generic, unpersonalized message.
      
      
        Sahar was only present two or three days a week, and
        when she was there, she acted as a
        stressed-out waitress, not a manager, unavailable, and
        never proactively communicative.
      

      
        I was never invited to discuss my role or expectations. I was just a
        dishwasher, and she was the boss.
        She never introduced herself. .
      
      
        From the outset, I quickly realised I had no clear
        point of contact.
      

      
        She never asked me how I was doing.I never received an
        invitation to discuss problems or expectations with her.
        She gave me basic instructions‚Äîsuch as keeping the
        hotel corridor clean‚Äîbut
        never engaged in any managerial dialogue.
      

      
        Henrik (the chef) gave me practical instructions early
        on, like where to put the trash and where to get cleaning supplies. He
        was courteous, distant but always respectful.
      

      
        Sub-chefs quickly showed limits. They helped with small
        tasks but their body language made it clear not to insist. I stopped
        asking them anything beyond essentials.
      

      
        So I stopped trying. I started talking more with the
        waiters. With a few exceptions,
        they were helpful and pleasant. The general vibe was
        good. People seemed happy to be there.
      

      
        There was laughter, music, a sense of energy. Even if
        Sahar created some tension sometimes (like firing a waitress in front of
        me), the team was mostly upbeat. I believe this was largely due to good
        salaries. One bartender even told me this was the best opportunity he‚Äôd
        found after years in the field.
      

      
        Only the waiters were approachable, mostly kind and
        supportive. There was a generally good atmosphere among staff‚Äîmany
        seemed happy, possibly due to decent pay and tips.
      

      
        I had no HR, no staff coordinator, and no one in a
        defined role to address workplace questions. The entire structure ran on
        proxy and inference.
      

      
        The result was clear: I had to manage on my own. I
        needed answers, but found no one to ask. Eventually I emailed the
        restaurant directly. No one contested this, but I could tell
        it wasn‚Äôt how things were supposed to be done. They had
        been looking for a dishwasher for months. I got positive feedback from
        many coworkers. Several told me I was doing a great job.
      
      
        Henrik, the co-gerant, was polite but distant. We
        exchanged maybe three words in three weeks. He showed interest in the
        music I listened to once, and that‚Äôs how I learned he spoke Japanese.
        He never introduced himself. Everything else I learned
        about him came from colleagues.
        At no point could I tell he had any managerial role.
      

      
        I tried to reach Sahar by email after an incident with cleaners I hadn‚Äôt
        been informed about. Her response confirmed the vague structure:
        <strong
          >I was offered to replace them, as if this was a known path</strong
        >.
      
      
        <strong
          >The management triangle (Sahar, Henrik, and the co-manager)</strong
        >
        was disconnected. They rarely spoke. I never once saw Sahar and Henrik
        (co-g√©rant) interact or stand side-by-side.
      
      
        Over time, I learned
        Sahar was married to the founder, who was best friends
        with Henrik. This lack of shared leadership permeated
        the workplace and made me rely on trial-and-error and informal channels
        to understand my role.
      

      
        It was only after a few days on site that I discovered the restaurant
        was legally operated by HSSC Event AB‚Äînot Quan, nor
        Elite Hotel. The name appeared in the internal scheduling platform
        Personalkollen, which employees used to access shift
        information.
      

      
        Despite this, quanbyquan.se has been actively used for
        internal communication. At least four domain-linked emails were
        confirmed as active: hs, se, hk, and sc@quanbyquan.se.
        Delivery receipts confirm messages reached these recipients.
      

      
        Henrik Kei Sieber, publicly introduced as the lead
        figure behind Quan, maintained a
        discreet yet regular presence. I observed him working
        no more than two to three days a week, typically welcoming guests and
        overseeing the front-of-house with focused attention.
      

      
        Two chefs, Robin Albay Dinopol and
        Satoru Yoshizawa, who were regularly scheduled on
        evening shifts, were later identified as the sole partners of
        BURI Handelsbolag (org.nr 969798-6447). Their company
        is not listed as a subcontractor, but they both worked onsite as cooks.
      

      
        This configuration raises the possibility of
        undeclared subcontracting, where staff are employed
        through a third-party vehicle without formal declaration. No document or
        contract was disclosed to clarify the terms of their engagement with
        Quan or HSSC Event AB.
      

      
        Another external subcontractor was regularly observed
        on site every Friday night. A cleaning couple arrived at approximately
        23:30 and remained on site until around
        04:00, working four hours each.
      

      
        Their presence accounted for a total of
        eight hours per session. They were not listed on any
        official schedule, and no company name or contractual arrangement was
        ever disclosed. Management suggested I might be asked to
        replace them due to dissatisfaction with their work.

Position Framework
Last updated: Wednesday, May 14, 2025 at 08:11 PM


      <details
        style="
          background-color: #e5e7eb;
          border-radius: 0.6rem;
          padding: 1.5rem;
          margin: 1.5rem 0;
          font-size: 0.96rem;
          line-height: 1.6;
        "
      >
        
          üß† Definitions and Use Cases
        

        üìå Position Paper
        
          
            Definition: A position paper is a
            concise document that
            clearly states a position on a specific issue. It
            typically includes:
            
              an analysis of the facts,
              a justified stance,
              recommendations or future perspectives.
            
          
          
            Contexts of use:
            
              
                Diplomatic and political: to express the stance
                of a state or party on a treaty or conflict.
              
              
                Business and NGOs: to position publicly on
                controversial issues (climate, labor, social justice, etc.).
              
              
                Academia: often part of legal, political
                science, or economics coursework.
              
              
                Advocacy journalism: in activist blogs or union
                media to defend causes.
              
            
          
          
            Translations: Position Note or
            Position Document.
            Sometimes also: Engaged Analysis, Critical Brief,
            or Public Stand.
          
          
            Relevance for this blog: Very high. It doesn‚Äôt just
            narrate; it takes a stand on a social or legal dysfunction. This
            hybrid format combines analysis, testimony,
            grievance, and methodical breakdown.
          
        

        
          üñãÔ∏è Editorial Framework
        
        
          
            Definition: An editorial framework is a
            writing and publishing framework that defines:
            
              the editorial intent of the site,
              its methodology (tone, structure, form),
              the criteria for topic selection,
              and the reading grid suggested to the audience.
            
          
          
            Contexts of use:
            
              
                Journalistic environments: to define the
                editorial line and logic.
              
              
                Legal or documentary platforms: to clarify
                scope and method for critical readers.
              
            
          
        

        <div
          style="
            margin-top: 1em;
            padding-top: 0.5em;
            border-top: 1px solid #ccc;
          "
        >
          
            ‚û§ This hybrid title was chosen to reflect both the argumentative
            rigor of a position paper and the narrative scaffolding of an
            editorial framework.
          
        
      
      
        The Unsocial Hours is a
        tactical-legal journal born out of systematic
        communication failure. From the first to the last shift, the employment
        relationship was marked by lack of transparency, lack
        of guidance, and the absence of any formal framework.
      
      
        This ongoing blog documents and analyzes a workplace where
        legitimate requests for clarity or payment were
        increasingly met with silence or
        hostility.
      

      
        The journal was initiated following a
        dishwasher dismissal without a written contract, and
        remains active.
      
      
        The last interaction with the employer took place in
        mid-April 2025, when a counter-offer ‚Äî equivalent to
        two weeks of salary ‚Äî was made in an attempt to preempt a formal legal
        claim.
      

      <p
        style="
          background-color: #f0f0f0;
          padding: 1.2em;
          border-radius: 10px;
          font-size: 0.95rem;
          line-height: 1.6;
        "
      >
        This blog offers a personal investigation into a real
        labor conflict I experienced as a dishwasher in late 2024. Each post
        analyzes a key incident ‚Äî such as a
        dismissal by SMS ‚Äî and
        explores the
        legal, procedural, and ethical implications
        involved.
        It also provides a structured timeline of events,
        highlights contractual breaches and
        administrative irregularities, and reviews the
        legal obligations potentially violated.
        The approach combines factual narration,
        legal interpretation, and
        socio-professional reflection, to identify broader
        structural failures and accountability gaps.
      
      
        <strong
          >This blog functions as a public legal and editorial framework</strong
        >, anchored in labor law terminology and socio-professional analysis. It
        is also a space of
        personal training and experimentation ‚Äî an initiation
        into legal reasoning, narrative structure, and stylistic clarity.
      

      
        Through this evolving exercise, it seeks to
        clarify damages, surface deeper conflict mechanisms,
        and outline actionable legal paths.
      

      
        The Unsocial Hours also serves as a pragmatic space for
        defense, documentation, and strategic anticipation in
        the face of opaque or hostile work environments.
      

      
        It seeks to
        <strong
          >echo the voice of those in the shadows of the labor market</strong
        >, especially in roles marked by high turnover, low visibility, or
        informal contracts ‚Äî such as
        dishwashing and other back-of-house positions.
      
      
        Rather than merely narrate, this journal encourages
        cross-reference and pattern recognition ‚Äî inviting
        comparisons, shared learning, and structured forms of response. It also
        aims to
        federate workers, legal minds, and isolated cases
        around common practices.
      
      
        A dedicated Contact & Collaboration Page invites
        legal professionals, labor advisors, and independent contributors. See
        also the
        forum manifesto
        for collective principles.
      

      
        The Unsocial Hours examines practical ways to engage
        legal standards through writing, structure, and visibility ‚Äî especially
        in contexts where formal procedures are slow, unclear, or inaccessible.
        It encourages adaptive methods to address legal silence and aims to make
        labor justice more responsive to lived realities.
      

      <div
        style="
          background-color: #f0f0f0;
          padding: 1.2em;
          border-radius: 10px;
          font-size: 0.95rem;
          line-height: 1.6;
        "
      >
        
          About the title: The Unsocial Hours refers
          to late shifts and
          marginal work schedules, often excluded from
          mainstream labor protections.
        
        
          This expression echoes the Swedish term
          ‚Äúobekv√§m arbetstid‚Äù (literally:
          ‚Äúinconvenient working hours‚Äù), which inspired the
          initials ‚ÄúOB‚Äù. The journal title is both
          a nod to this legal category, and
          <strong
            >a reflection on how those hours often lead to social invisibility,
            legal opacity, and managerial impunity</strong
          >.
        
        
          You can read more in the
          <a
            href="/glossary.html#unsocial-hours"
            style="text-decoration: underline"
            >glossary entry</a
          >.

      Context
      
        
          This part introduces the narrative grid ‚Äî a
          pragmatic label for a three-part structure designed
          to trace key stages of a workplace conflict through structured
          narrative blocks.
        
        
          
            üß© Part 1 ‚Äî Narrative Structure of Fact
          

          
            Function: This section explains
            how, when, and
            under what intent I entered the situation ‚Äî by
            laying out the
            conditions, sequence, and strategic meaning that
            preceded the conflict.
          

          
            Fields: This kind of structure appears as a
            case chronology (legal), a
            mission log (ops), or an
            incident report (HR). Comparable formats exist in
            investigative journalism and
            strategic consulting (as practiced by firms like McKinsey,
            EY, or KPMG).
          

          
            Usage: Lawyers, auditors, and compliance agents use
            such forms to detect
            managerial drift,
            accountability gaps,
            or signs of
            proxy communication
            in hierarchical systems.
          

          
            Adaptation: This structure serves as a form of
            early positioning. It anticipates legal tactics aiming to minimize
            damage by framing the claimant as incoherent, fragile, or unserious.
          

          
            Structure: The narrative follows a strict
            3-paragraph model: intent, chronology, and strategic framing. It
            presents no claim and no emotion ‚Äî only a foundation.
          

          
            üìö Continue the grid:
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/working-dynamics.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 2 ‚Äì Process Narative</a
            >
            ‚§∑
            <a href="/governance.html#narrative-intro"
              >Part 3 ‚Äì Authority Mapping</a
            >
          
        
      
      
        I arrived in Sweden in April 2022, first in Gothenburg, then in
        Stockholm. I worked for 14 months at
        Da Peppe Due</strong
        >, a pizzeria where I earned up to
        <strong
          ><a
            href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1dgAYR3CPEaqNFUOpsShy7LYe7sNq49jW/view?usp=sharing"
            >28,000 SEK net</a
          ></strong
        >
        per month, enjoyed free meals, and operated in a flexible environment.
      

      
        Before moving to Sweden, I mostly worked in
        <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/patrice-kenmo%C3%A9-a27236207"
          >technical support</a
        >
        and IT operations
        roles across Europe ‚Äî sometimes with
        partial engineering or
        coordination responsibilities. This was the first time
        I had held a truly subordinate position for so long. And after a full
        year, despite the salary and decent conditions, the role had become
        morally exhausting.
      

      
        I had regained everything I needed materially after nearly a decade of
        precariousness. I had secured eligibility for unemployment benefits. But
        remaining a dishwasher any longer would have meant
        accepting a symbolic label I could no longer carry. The second phase of
        my strategy had to begin.
      

      
        In May 2024, after a breakup, I entered a period of
        <strong
          ><a
            href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1rtj9b9BVrquGxQHegjPrs6o0ZP-9BRoR/view?usp=sharing"
            >housing precarity</a
          ></strong
        >
        in Stockholm. I no longer had stable shelter, but I retained 24/7 access
        to a coworking space. The following month, in June, I
        worked in two restaurants and earned 32,000 SEK‚Äîmy
        highest official monthly income.
      

      
        Despite this, the city's
        stress, noise, and compressed energy had become too
        much. I needed calmer surroundings, both socially and mentally.
        Malm√∂ offered a logical reset: softer social dynamics,
        fewer frictions, and a milder climate‚Äîone I knew would be safer to
        endure if housing became uncertain again.
      

      
        This marked the start of Phase Two: securing the final
        tools for tech entrepreneurship. I aimed to acquire a
        car, an ultra-wide monitor, a backup laptop, and
        <strong
          ><a
            href="https://verksamt.se/en/setting-up/choose-business-type/limited-company"
            >25,000 SEK in incorporation funds</a
          ></strong
        >. Once covered, Phase Three‚Äîbuilding the company‚Äîcould
        begin.
      
      
        I arrived in Malm√∂ on November 1, 2024, determined to
        resume work in a higher-standard kitchen. I shortlisted venues with
        top-rated service reviews, hoping to find a place where
        my obsessive attention to detail would be seen as an asset‚Äînot a flaw,
        as in my last job.
      
      
        On November 16, I sent a spontaneous application to
        Quan. I was aware the restaurant was attached to a
        hotel, but only during my trial shift did I fully realize the extent of
        its integration within a 4-star hotel.
      

      
        Many of my early questions‚Äîabout dishware, trolleys, or food
        storage‚Äîwere answered with ‚Äúit‚Äôs for the hotel.‚Äù I deduced that the
        entire food and conference service, including breakfast, was run by the
        same company, but no clear onboarding ever explained these overlaps. The
        structure remained opaque.
      
      
        
          <a
            href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1s6uTnBQCgQGC0qQVsxj-ili6KFA7bZ1/view?usp=sharing"
            >around 2 PM</a
          >
        
      

      
        Her familiarity felt disproportionate coming from someone I‚Äôd never met.
        I responded politely but awkwardly, unsure who she was. When she and
        Henrik entered the meeting room together, she naturally led the
        conversation. That‚Äôs when I assumed she was
        in charge of the restaurant‚Äîsomeone with practical
        authority beyond her official title.
      

      
        No one introduced her or confirmed her title. Later, colleagues casually
        referred to her as ‚Äúthe boss.‚Äù I had no reason to doubt it. I
        only discovered much later she was
        formally listed as Deputy Board Member‚Äîa position that
        carries no formal management authority in Sweden.
      

      
        That gap between perceived authority and official status didn‚Äôt strike
        me immediately, but it shaped a subtle confusion. I adapted to her
        leadership as if she were the founder or legal manager. At no point was
        I told otherwise.
      

      
        That ambiguity had immediate consequences: moments earlier, I had
        greeted several team members, including a
        floor manager I‚Äôd bonded with during my shift. He
        ignored my handshake. In retrospect, I interpreted this as a reaction to
        my rushed greeting to her‚Äîpossibly seen as a
        lack of deference to the executive lead.
      

      
        The session itself was warm.
        Henrik showed visible enthusiasm, while Sahar remained
        measured but positive. Both seemed relieved to have found someone
        ‚Äúreliable‚Äù. I, too, felt I had landed in the right place,
        though I sensed a slight mismatch between Sahar‚Äôs informal posture and
        the authority she embodied.
      
      
        The tone was enthusiastic. They expressed visible relief at finding
        someone ‚Äúreliable.‚Äù They emphasized three principles:
        punctuality, exclusive availability,
        and attention to detail‚Äîframed as missing virtues in
        their previous hires.
      

      
        I was offered an hourly rate of 160 SEK/h on the spot,
        based on my CV and the trial performance. I disclosed an existing
        weekend job, which Sahar acknowledged without hesitation, even framing
        it as a sign of integrity.
      

      
        During that meeting,
        Sahar mentioned a digital contract would be sent. I
        expected it within days, but no document ever arrived. No login
        credentials, no confirmation, no follow-up. The promise remained
        unfulfilled despite clear mutual agreement.
      

      
        I also raised a condition: receiving a share of tips.
        They said the matter would be discussed with the floor and bar managers.
        A few days later, both confirmed their approval individually. No
        contract followed, but Sahar briefly mentioned one would‚Äîpossibly via
        their internal system. That mention was never repeated.
      
      
        Throughout this period,
        my only point of contact was Henrik. His number was the
        only one I received. Any attempt to address questions or follow up‚Äîabout
        schedules, duties, or documents‚Äîwas redirected:
        ‚ÄúI'll ask Sahar.‚Äù Eventually,
        I stopped asking. He often seemed embarrassed or
        reluctant.
      

      
        When he was absent, I was told to ask the sous-chefs.
        That proved even more difficult. Their responses felt dismissive, and I
        quickly sensed that pushing further was unwelcome. I
        began submitting written questions to the restaurant‚Äôs general email.
        These were not challenged, but I knew
        they fell outside accepted channels.
      

      
        The meeting lasted approximately 30 minutes, between
        13:53 and 14:28, as confirmed in my Google Timeline.
        Though informal in tone, it set the
        essential terms of work and gave rise to what I
        interpreted as the start of formal employment.

      >
        
          Chronology of the Events (Nov 23 - Dec 28)
        
        
          Between 23&nbsp;Nov&nbsp;2024 and
          28&nbsp;Dec&nbsp;2025 a rapid‚Äëfire
          chain of events transformed an ordinary kitchen job into a public
          labour dispute.
        
        
          This page will soon display a day‚Äëby‚Äëday timeline of
          that period‚Äîshift notes, e‚Äëmails, calls and decisive moments‚Äîeach
          summed up in a clean card you can browse or filter.
        
        
          The aim is clarity: helping readers place every article and
          legal analysis in context before forming their own view.
        
        First public release coming shortly. Stay tuned.

      Legacy Foundations of Quan
      
        
          üß≠ Methodology & Disciplines Used in This Chronology
        
      
        This investigation relies on a multidisciplinary approach combining law, governance, financial tracing, and structural genealogy. It draws from investigative methods used in legal forensics, compliance auditing, and influence mapping.
      
        
          Corporate Genealogy: Tracks ownership succession, entity transitions, and long-term structural transfers (e.g., control, naming, rights).
          Forensic History: Reconstructs undocumented events or turning points using official traces and first-hand narratives.
          Shadow Governance: Reveals who holds practical power or makes key decisions without being formally listed on legal records.
          Forensic Accounting: Analyzes capital flows, internal loans, and suspicious asset shifts‚Äîoften used in compliance or cross-ownership audits.
          POWER(E) Method: A diagnostic tool that assesses control through 5+1 angles ‚Äî Properties, Operations, Wallets, Employees, Reputation.
          Liability Mapping: Helps determine who actually holds legal and reputational risk in hybrid or shared-governance companies.
        
      
        üìå These frameworks allow us to map who acts, who controls, who profits, and who represents ‚Äî even when paper trails suggest otherwise. Especially relevant in cases involving family businesses, founder-linked ventures, or parallel ownership networks.
      
      
        What would later become Quan emerged 30 years ago at Lilla Torg, driven by Henrik Siebert ‚Äî concept development and Asian cuisine ‚Äî and Saahil Chudasama, who ensured legal and structural grounding. Neither could have done it alone.
      
      
        Thereafter ‚Äî July 25, 1990 ‚Äì Michael Hagqvist (21) incorporates Etagegruppen AB (556402-6697) to run the Malm√∂ nightclub Etage, launching what will become a regional hospitality group.
      
      
      
        Years later, the company will absorb a key venue ‚Äî quietly closing the founding phase shaped by their combined efforts.
      

      
        May 19, 1991, Jayantil Chudasama (46)
        establishes the current format of the restaurant later
        known as Steakhouse Lilla Torg. In 1994, he
        officially registers the name. His son Saahil (14) is
        present during this period,
        <mark style="background-color: #e0e0e0"
          >a family that would later play a key role in Henrik‚Äôs journey</mark
        >.
      

      April 16, 1993 ‚Äî Just a few meters away, mixed Japanese‚ÄìSwedish brothers Toni (26) and Ronnie Petersson (22) open Izakaya Koi. They introduce the izakaya (Japanese pub) concept to Scania, blending sushi bar, DJ sets, and lounge energy into a nightlife format still rare in Sweden.

      The venue is split across two levels: a street-level restaurant with a terrace, and an upstairs cocktail bar and dancefloor. It quickly became a trendy nightlife spot in Malm√∂.

      üìå 2004
      
        On November 19, Henrik is officially
        registered as a Board Member of
        IZAKAYAKOI Aktiebolag (556462-5761) ‚Äî the original
        corporate entity behind Izakaya Koi's first iteration. He remains listed
        until the company‚Äôs liquidation in 2011, marking the
        legal end of this structure.
      
      
        At that time, the board consists of only two individuals: Henrik as
        Board Member, and a second person as
        Deputy Board Member. In addition, the structure includes one
        Auditor and one Deputy Auditor.
      
      üìç 2006

      
        On the night of 12 October 2006 at 3 a.m., during a
        study trip to London, a violent altercation occurred between
        Henrik Siebert and kitchen employee
        Frej S√∂derberg at a nightclub.
        Saahil Chudasama, not officially employed but close to
        the team, intervened physically.
      

      
        Employee Daniela Dahl, later registered at the same
        address as Henrik and eventually listed on the company‚Äôs board, was also
        present. The incident led to Frej‚Äôs dismissal shortly after the group
        returned to Malm√∂.
      

      
        On 1 December, 26 members of the
        SAC union staged a public blockade of the restaurant.
        The protest led to a collective trial in
        September 2007 at Malm√∂ District Court.
      

      üìå 2007
      
        üìÑ On December 31, the
        <a href="/documents/Annual_report_2007-12-31.pdf" target="_blank"
          >Annual Report</a
        >
        shows a shift in trajectory: turnover reaches 10.99M SEK, but the
        company records a loss of ‚àí248K SEK.
      
      
        <strong
          >The decline in profit following a record surplus the year
          before</strong
        >
        raises concerns of
        <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
          >artificial earnings inflation or concealed cash outflows</span
        >.
      
      
        Governance remains minimal: Henrik is the only Board Member, joined only
        by a Deputy Board Member and a formal audit pair.
        <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
          >No operational management is documented</span
        >.
      
      üìç 2008

      
        On 16 January 2008, the Swedish Labour Court ruled that
        Frej S√∂derberg was lawfully dismissed for serious misconduct after
        initiating a physical altercation.
      

      
        The court acknowledged legal violations by the employer and awarded:
        15,000 SEK for procedural breach (lack of written
        notice and union consult), and 5,000 SEK for failure to
        issue a written contract.
      
      
        The SAC union was ordered to pay 139,000 SEK in legal
        fees, to reimburse the opposing party‚Äôs litigation and attorney costs.
      

      
        On 26 November 2008, Realtid reported
        that Skatteverket had frozen
        Izakaya Koi‚Äôs bank accounts and revoked its alcohol
        license due to massive bookkeeping fraud. Estimated tax debt reached
        905,780 SEK.
      

      
        On 9 December,
        Izakayakoi Aktiebolag became
        Chip-Chop mat AB. That same day, a new entity,
        Izakayakoi AB, was registered at
        c/o Restaurang Steakhouse Lilla Torg, linked to the
        Chudasama family.
      

      
        The company‚Äôs board included both
        Jayantilal Chudasama (age ~63) as Chairman and his son
        Alexander Saahil Chudasama as Director, confirming
        direct father‚Äìson involvement.
      

      
        Around 17 December, Izakayakoi AB was
        granted a new serving license, shortly after being restructured under a
        different legal entity with new representatives.
      

      
        On 19 December, media reports revealed that
        Skatteverket had uncovered unreported earnings linked to
        Izakayakoi AB, used to finance personal luxury
        expenses, including high-end shopping in London and New York.
      

      
        The owner was reported to have spent
        1.1 million SEK from undeclared income between 2006 and
        2008. Skatteverket considered these funds to be disguised salary income
        not declared or taxed correctly.
      
      üìç 2009

      
        On 18 February,
        Chip-Chop mat AB officially changed its name to
        Yakisoba AB and simultaneously moved its registered
        office to Slottsgatan 12, 211 22 Malm√∂, consolidating
        its legal and administrative identity under a new structure.
      

      
        On 9 May, former Izakayakoi owner
        Henrik Siebert was formally suspected of two financial
        crimes, following a deep audit by Skatteverket
        targeting cash register manipulation and undeclared revenues.
      

      
        Prosecutors stated that the alleged offenses could result in up to six
        years in prison. According to court filings, the case was still in early
        stages at the time.
      
      üìç 2010

      
        On 8 August, a 34-year-old tourist was found
        unconscious after an altercation with Izakaya Koi‚Äôs security staff.
        Police opened an investigation for assault.
      

      
        On June 18, the five-star Renaissance Hotel Malm√∂ opens its doors ‚Äî the first Marriott-branded location in Sweden. Operated by Luxury Hotels International Sweden AB (org. no. 559182-9386), the hotel is based at M√§ster Johansgatan 15, where Quan will later operate.
        
      
        
          The hotel features the Rosen Bar & Dining, a venue known for blending contemporary Swedish cuisine with Spanish influences, focused on seasonal and local ingredients.
          

      üìç 2011

      
        On 28 April 2011,
        Yakisoba AB (formerly known as
        Izakayakoi Aktiebolag) was formally declared in
        liquidation. This marked the legal end of the original corporate entity
        behind Izakaya Koi.
      
      
        üìç 2012
      
      

        On January 17, Saahil Chudasama (32)
        commissions the creation of a company named
        Saahil AB via
        Bolagsstiftarna, a
        Swedish shelf company provider. A month
        later, Sahar (32) is formally added as deputy board
        member ‚Äî
        her first trace in the corporate structures orbiting Quan.
      

      
        On January 19, the property housing the Renaissance Hotel Malm√∂ is acquired for 400 MSEK by Fastighets AB Balder (org. no. 556525-6905). The real estate transfer concerns the Rosen 9 property at M√§ster Johansgatan 15, while Marriott remains tenant-operator under lease.
        

        
          On April 13, the Companies Registration Office officially records a board and address change for IzakayaKoi AB (556765-3844). Michael Hagqvist (42), CEO of Etagegruppen AB (556402-6697), is appointed as sole administrator, with his wife Emmy listed as deputy member. This update formalizes the full integration of IzakayaKoi into the Etagegruppen structure.
          
          
          
          The company‚Äôs official address is simultaneously changed to c/o Etagegruppen AB, Stortorget 6, 211 34 Malm√∂, directly aligning its operations with the group‚Äôs headquarters. From this point onward, IzakayaKoi AB becomes a wholly owned subsidiary of Etagegruppen AB, marking the end of the Peterson era and a strategic absorption into a new corporate lineage.

          üìå Note ‚Äî Auditor Appointment Requirement in Sweden
        

        
          Under Swedish law (√Örsredovisningslagen), limited companies
          must appoint a statutory auditor if they exceed
          2 out of 3 thresholds for
          two consecutive years:
        

        
          
            
              Criterion
              Threshold
              Typical Source
            
          
          
            
              Balance sheet total
              > 1.5 MSEK
              Annual report or credit report
            
            
              Net turnover
              > 3 MSEK
              Annual report or credit report
            
            
              Employees (average)
              > 3
              Skatteverket or credit report
            
          
        

        
          In the case of HSSC Event AB, the 2023 credit report
          shows the following growth trajectory:
        

        
          2021 ‚Üí 11.3 MSEK turnover
          2022 ‚Üí 22.9 MSEK
          2023 ‚Üí 40.5 MSEK, with 21 employees
        

        
          üßæ Conclusion ‚Äî If the company had >3 employees and
          >3 MSEK in turnover as early as 2020 (likely given the curve), it
          triggered the legal obligation to appoint an auditor by
          2021.
        

        
          Its appointment on 10 May 2021 may reflect a
          late compliance adjustment ‚Äî a common occurrence among
          fast-scaling private firms. Not a scandal, but a useful forensic
          marker.
        
      
      
        üìé Note ‚Äî Role of a Holding Company
        
          A holding company is a legal structure created to
          own shares in one or more other companies, often without any
          direct operational activity. Its primary purpose is to
          consolidate control and centralize profits, typically through
          the reception of dividends.
        
        
          In Sweden, this structure is widely used for
          tax optimization: profits received by the holding are
          usually tax-exempt, and personal income from dividends can be deferred
          or distributed under more favorable tax brackets (typically
          20‚Äì30% under the ‚Äú3:12 rules‚Äù).
        
        
          This setup is legal and common, especially among entrepreneurs
          and founders. However, when combined with
          limited transparency, it can make it harder to identify the
          true financial beneficiaries behind a company‚Äôs profits.
        
      
      
        üìé Note ‚Äî Property & Asset Manager

        
          A property & asset manager is a type of company that
          doesn't sell anything or run a daily business. Instead, it's often
          used to
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >own things (like real estate or shares)</span
          >
          and get paid from them.
        

        
          For example, some restaurateurs use one company to run the restaurant,
          and
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >another company to own the building</span
          >
          or receive rent. This setup can also help
          finance a personal apartment or protect family
          property.
        

        
          It's a common and legal structure, especially when
          people want to separate risk and income, or when they want to
          pay themselves differently ‚Äî not as salary, but through other
          income.
        
      
      
        üìå Note ‚Äî What‚Äôs an ‚ÄúInvest AB‚Äù?

        
          The ‚ÄúInvest AB‚Äù suffix ‚Äî short for
          Investment Aktiebolag ‚Äî doesn‚Äôt always imply an active
          investment firm. In Swedish business practice, it often means a
          company used for
          holding, shielding, or managing income through a
          separate legal structure.
        

        
          The model is popular among restaurateurs and service professionals.
          Instead of drawing a salary (which is taxed at a higher rate), they
          channel earnings into their Invest AB, pay lower corporate tax, and
          later withdraw dividends at favorable rates.
        

        
          In Malm√∂‚Äôs hospitality scene, dozens of ‚ÄúInvest AB‚Äù entities serve to
          buy family apartments, own restaurant buildings, or
          simply shield liability. It‚Äôs a quiet way of
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            ><strong
              >separating private control from operational exposure</strong
            ></span
          >.
        

        
          This strategy gained traction post-2006 tax reforms in Sweden, and is
          now a common template for service-heavy or risk-prone sectors.
        
        
        
          Key external sources ‚Äî to explore the fiscal roots of
          Invest AB strategies:
