        ‚ú± Note ‚Äì Location Proximity
        
          Izakaya Koi is officially registered at
          Lilla Torg 5, while
          Steakhouse Lilla Torg and the Indian restaurant
          Green Chili both list Lilla Torg 7.
          According to Malm√∂'s registry and street layout, the three venues are
          only meters apart, with Green Chili positioned directly between the
          two. This makes them effectively adjacent and highly exposed to each
          other‚Äôs clientele.
        
      
      
        
          üìå Note ‚Äî What‚Äôs a ‚ÄúShelf Company Provider‚Äù?
        

        
          In Sweden, a shelf company provider refers to a firm
          that pre-registers companies (typically ABs) with
          Bolagsverket and keeps them dormant until purchased. These
          off-the-shelf structures come with an
          active organization number,
          clean corporate history, and zero prior
          operations.
        

        
          This setup allows buyers to
          bypass registration delays and operate
          immediately. It's commonly used in
          legal restructurings, ownership transitions,
          or to ensure founder anonymity at
          incorporation.
        

        
          One of the best-known Swedish providers is
          Bolagsstiftarna</strong
          >, based in G√∂teborg. They offer ready-to-use ABs, allow for
          fast name changes, and can include
          proxy board members on request ‚Äî making them ideal for discreet
          setups.
        

        üïµÔ∏è Discretion ‚Äî Minimal paper trail, no publicity
        
          
            Dissociate identity from registration timeline
          
          
            Bypass public founder records and
            reduce paper trail
          
          Protect strategic intentions during sensitive launches
        

        ‚ö° Speed ‚Äî Same-day activation, legal status already granted
        
          
            Legal entity is already active with share capital
            in place
          
          
            Contracts, subleases, bank accounts can be processed within
            24‚Äì48h
          
          
            Avoid 2‚Äì3 week setup delays of
            standard routes
          
        

        
          üß© Repositioning ‚Äî Branding flexibility and structural remapping
        
        
          
            Rename instantly to reflect new identity or investment use
          
          
            Recycle dormant ABs for fresh legal
            wrappers
          
          
            Shield the rebranding process from competitors or
            institutions
          
        
      
      
        
          ‚öñÔ∏è Note ‚Äì Beneficial Ownership Transparency
        
        
          Under EU Directive 2015/849 on anti-money laundering,
          Swedish companies must identify their verklig huvudman (<u
            >beneficial owner</u
          >) separately from board representatives. This rule aims to
          prevent opaque control structures
          and ensure transparency in corporate governance.
        
        
          Since 2017, all Aktiebolag must
          report their beneficial owners via
          <a
            href="https://bolagsverket.se/en/us/about/our-services/beneficial-owner"
            class="subtle-link"
            target="_blank"
          >
            Bolagsverket's official register</a
          >. Non-compliance may lead to administrative sanctions or even
          criminal investigation
          under Swedish economic crime law.
        
        
          üìÑ Official text:
          <a
            href="https://eur-lex.europa.eu/legal-content/EN/TXT/?uri=CELEX%3A32015L0849"
            class="subtle-link"
            target="_blank"
          >
            EU Directive 2015/849 ‚Äì EUR-Lex</a
          >
        
      
      
        
          <strong
            >‚öñÔ∏è Note ‚Äì Legal Disclosure Obligations for Commercial
            Websites</strong
          >
        
        
          Most jurisdictions‚Äîincluding Sweden‚Äîrequire commercial websites to
          identify their legal operator. In Sweden, this is enforced by the
          E-commerce Act (2002:562), which mandates clear
          display of the company name, organisation number, VAT ID, and
          contact details.
        
        
          This transparency
          protects consumers and employees,
          facilitates accountability, and ensures traceability of online
          businesses. Similar obligations exist across the EU, Germany
          (Impressumspflicht), and France (mentions l√©gales).
        
        
          Omission of such disclosures is not always illegal, but it typically
          indicates
          informal structuring or intent to limit visibility‚Äî<u
            >which can obstruct due diligence</u
          >
          or legal recourse in case of dispute.
        
      
      
        
          ‚öñÔ∏è Note ‚Äî Board Member vs. Effective Owner
        

        
          In Swedish company law, a
          board member (styrelseledamot) is the official legal
          figure associated with governance. But in practice, this role is often
          used to signal legitimacy or
          front a corporate structure
          without reflecting who truly controls the business.
        

        
          According to EU Directive 2015/849, the
          beneficial owner (verklig huvudman) must be disclosed
          separately ‚Äî typically the person who ultimately owns or controls the
          entity. This aims to
          prevent opacity and deter misuse of
          legal facades.
        

        
          In sectors like hospitality or nightlife, it‚Äôs common to find
          proxy board members (e.g. family, accountant,
          long-time friend) while real power is exercised by someone else ‚Äî
          often due to reputation concerns, past legal trouble, or the
          need to stay out of public documents.
        

        
          In the case of HHSC Event AB, for instance, Mr.
          Henrik Siebert, widely acknowledged as a key architect of the
          Quan project, does
          not appear in any official filing.
          Instead, Saahil Chudasama and Sahar El Nasser are listed, while the
          beneficial owner is Ms. Dahl.
        

        
          This discrepancy suggests a
          protective distancing strategy:
          separating operational control from legal exposure. In cases
          like these, the board may reflect not power, but cover.
        
      
      
        
          <strong
            >‚öñÔ∏è Note ‚Äî Proxy Governance & Hidden Control in Hospitality
            Deals</strong
          >
        

        
          In many hospitality ventures,
          board members listed in legal filings are not the
          actual initiators or operators. Instead, they often act as
          legal proxies for visibility-sensitive founders, allowing for
          discretion, operational distancing, or reputational shielding.
        

        
          The case of
          <span class="highlight"
            >Henrik Siebert‚Äôs absence from the board of HSSC Event AB</span
          >, despite his public role in launching Quan, points to a likely
          strategy of protective distancing. This setup enables
          the true initiator to
          control strategy and execution from the background, while
          ensuring no formal tie appears in commercial registries.
        

        
          In high-end properties‚Äîespecially those operating under
          Marriott International or
          Elite Hotels of Sweden‚Äîsuch distancing may even be
          required. Large hotel groups often conduct internal vetting and
          avoid contracting with individuals involved in prior disputes,
          reputational risk, or internal conflicts. This can lead to private
          conditions requiring founders to remain out of legal view, using
          ‚Äúclean‚Äù board members as interface.
        

        
          While not inherently illegal, this practice blurs the lines between
          ownership, control, and liability. It can be used to obscure
          lines of accountability and delay consequences in case of legal
          disputes, financial mismanagement, or employee claims.
        

        
          In Sweden, the 2015 EU directive on money laundering requires
          companies to register a
          verklig huvudman (beneficial owner), separate from
          the board, to limit such opacity. Yet in practice,
          <u
            >many shelf-company setups or private agreements still allow
            circumvention</u
          >, especially in small or family-run ventures.

        üìå Note ‚Äì Etagegruppen AB: From Club Etage to Malm√∂'s Nightlife Empire
        
          Etagegruppen AB (org.¬†556402-6697) is a regional hospitality group founded on July 25, 1990 by Michael Hagqvist (21), to operate the Malm√∂ nightclub Etage, located at Stortorget¬†6. The venue, originally opened in the 1980s, became one of the largest clubs in the city with 4 dance floors and a karaoke bar, and has remained an iconic nightlife spot.
        
        
          During the 2000s, Etagegruppen expanded its footprint in Malm√∂ with a portfolio including:
          
            Centiliter & Gram (created 2007, opened 2008) ‚Äì a premium cocktail bar (Stortorget¬†17), popular among the 25+ crowd;
            Goose Bar & Restaurang (launched 2010) ‚Äì a casual pub-restaurant near Gustav Adolfs Torg;
            Club operations at Hotel Scandic Crown ‚Äì under the names Level (mainstream) and Wonk (LGBT+), active since 2011.
          
          By 2012, the group simultaneously managed Etage, Centiliter & Gram, Goose, and Level/Wonk, employing cross-venue synergies in marketing, ticketing, and HR.
        
        
          In April 2012, Etagegruppen acquired Izakaya Koi AB (556765-3844), absorbing its operational structure but preserving its original name and atmosphere. This marked the closure of the Henrik Siebert era and consolidated Etagegruppen‚Äôs control over key nightlife assets in Malm√∂‚Äôs central square.
        

        
          Etagegruppen‚Äôs reputation remains solid in Malm√∂‚Äôs nightlife scene. In 2013, its parent company posted revenues of ~5.5 million SEK (excluding subsidiaries), and its venues are regularly featured in nightlife guides. Hagqvist has also acted as a semi-official spokesperson for local business owners, including public opposition to restrictive terrace regulations.
        
  
      

      
        Swedish law (<a href="https://lagen.nu/2002:562#P8S1" target="_blank"
          >Act 2002:562</a
        >) requires hospitality sites to disclose a VAT number, legal operator,
        and contact. Over

  // Script pour la sidebar
  const toggleBtn = document.getElementById("toggleNavbar");
  const navbar = document.querySelector(".navbar");
  toggleBtn?.addEventListener("click", () => {
    navbar.classList.toggle("collapsed");
  });

  // Script pour injecter le footer
  fetch("/components/footer.html")
    .then(res => res.text())
    .then(html => {
      const footerContainer = document.createElement("div");
      footerContainer.innerHTML = html;
      document.body.appendChild(footerContainer);
    });

      The Emergence of a Model
      Outsourced Neo-Asian Restauranting
      <details
        open
        style="
          background-color: #e5e7eb;
          border-radius: 0.6rem;
          padding: 1.5rem;
          margin: 1.5rem 0;
          font-size: 0.96rem;
          line-height: 1.6;
        "
      >
        
          Liability Mapping (Hybrid Restaurant Governance)
        
        
          Function: This mapping helps clarify
          <strong
            >who acts, who decides, and who holds legal responsibility</strong
          >
          within Quan‚Äôs operational structure. It highlights overlaps between
          ownership, delegation, and public-facing control.
        

        
          PPOWER(E) Method

          
            The PPOWER(E) method is a simple tool to figure out who really
            controls a business ‚Äî not just on paper, but in practice. It‚Äôs used
            when official ownership doesn‚Äôt match what‚Äôs actually happening on
            the ground.
          

          
            The name stands for six key things to check. If one person or group
            shows up on most of them, they‚Äôre likely in charge ‚Äî even if they
            don‚Äôt legally ‚Äúown‚Äù anything.
          

          <table
            style="width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 0.95em"
          >
            
              
                Axis
                What to look for
              
            
            
              
                P ‚Äì Power
                
                  Who gives orders? Who takes the real decisions?
                
              
              
                P ‚Äì Property
                
                  Who owns it ‚Äî even indirectly or through someone else?
                
              
              
                O ‚Äì Operation
                
                  Who runs it day to day? Who shows up on site?
                
              
              
                W ‚Äì Wallet
                
                  Who receives payments? Who pays the bills?
                
              
              
                E ‚Äì Employees
                
                  Are staff shared across companies? Who hires them?
                
              
              
                R ‚Äì Reputation
                
                  Who is publicly seen as ‚Äúthe boss‚Äù or the face of the company?
                
              
            
          

          
            <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
              >In your case, this is useful to understand how HSSC, Aspircio,
              Queda Consulting and Tributum AB might be controlled by the same
              group ‚Äî without sharing official owners.</span
            >
          

          üìö Where does it come from?
          
            The method was first developed in the 2010s by financial
            investigators working on corruption and shell companies. It‚Äôs now
            used by investigative journalists, fraud examiners, and forensic
            analysts to spot real control hidden behind fake legal structures.
          
        
        
          Fields: Inspired by tools like a
          liability map (legal strategy),
          delegated ownership charts (corporate audits), and
          hybrid governance diagrams (used in
          hospitality outsourcing, franchise consulting, or
          operational compliance).
        
        
          Usage: Used by legal analysts,
          compliance teams (e.g. internal audit, regulatory
          staff), and governance advisors (e.g. strategic
          consultants for partnerships) to examine
          responsibility chains,
          control logic, and
          ownership/operation boundaries in co-managed
          ventures.
        
        
          Adaptation: This model is applied to
          clarify how responsibility was distributed without
          formal titles or clear legal attribution. It provides a lens to
          observe
          how tasks and decisions shifted between actors.
        
        
          Structure: The section highlights
          visible and latent hierarchies between hotel staff,
          branded leadership, and off-site owners. It distinguishes
          contractual obligations from
          day-to-day control ‚Äî to map where legal and
          operational authority may diverge.
        
      

      üìå 2015
      
        By 2015, Henrik is understood to have joined
        Renaissance Hotel Malm√∂ (then under
        Marriott branding). He gradually took over
        food and beverage operations, reportedly holding that
        role for two and a half years by 2018.
      

      üìå 2016

      üìé December 12, Saahil (36) restructures
      his personal company ‚Äî formerly known as Saahil AB
      (reg. no. 556881-0641) ‚Äî renaming it
      Chudasama Invest AB. The shift adopts the
      Invest AB
      format, signaling a transition from personal branding to structured asset
      holding.

      üìå 2018
      
        On February 1, 2018, following negotiations with
        Balder (556525-6905), the
        Elite Hotels of Sweden group (5562485259) secured the
        operating rights to the Renaissance Malm√∂ Hotel,
        replacing Marriott as operator.
      

      
        The dedicated subsidiary Elite Rosen Malm√∂ AB assumed
        control and temporarily rebranded the venue as
        Elite Hotel Adlon, a transitional identity during the
        franchise handover phase.
      

      
        üìÑ On June 25, a company
        HSSC Event AB (registration no.
        559163-2764) is officially registered in Malm√∂. Its
        name clearly reflects the initials of Henrik Siebert and
        Saahil Chudasama, who were both
        publicly presented as ‚Äúco-founders‚Äù of the Quan project</strong
        >.
      
      
        üìÑ The company,
        <strong
          >registered under the activity of restaurant and event
          services</strong
        >, lists M√§ster Johansgatan 15, Malm√∂ as its official
        address ‚Äî the same as the hotel hosting the Quan project.
      

      
      
        üìå All other companies introduced in this sequence are likewise
        legally domiciled at the same address, forming what is
        often referred to as a
        shared registration setup.
      

      
        üìë In the legal filings, Saahil Chudasama is declared
        as board member, and
        Sahar El Nasser as
        deputy board member.
        <em
          >No principal auditor is listed
          *.</em
        >
      
      
        üìé As shown in the beneficial ownership register,
        <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
          >Kehda Holding AB</span
        >
        ‚Äî holding between 50% and 75% of the company ‚Äî is controlled by
        Daniella Lin Dahl. Saahil Chudasama, via
        Chudasama Invest AB, holds less than 25% but retains
        strategic rights, including board control.
      

      
        ‚ö†Ô∏è Henrik Siebert does
        not appear in any official role at the time of HSSC Event AB‚Äôs
        registration (559163-2764), despite being publicly recognized as the
        face behind the Quan project. This visible absence may reflect a
        
          protective distancing strategy</a
        >, delegating legal appearances to proxies while retaining actual
        control in the background.
      

      üìå 2020

      
        üìÑ On 30 September, company no.
        559274-2042 is registered under the name KEHDA Holding
        AB. Its declared purpose is property and asset management,‚Ä¶with
        initial control held by
        Bolagsstiftarna appointees (as in 2012) ‚Äî all replaced
        weeks later by Daniella Lin Dahl.
      

      
        üìå Despite reporting
        no employees, clients, or listed assignments, KEHDA votes four
        consecutive profit distributions between 2021 and 2024,
        totaling over 1.2 million SEK. At least one appears
        linked to
        <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
          >strategic advisory billing from HSSC Event AB</span
        >, without itemized explanation.
      

      
        üß© The setup suggests a silent profit vehicle: KEHDA operates
        without public presence, while its sole representative shares a
        residence with Henrik Siebert. This may indicate a
        private holding layer,
        designed to channel earnings while shielding visible ownership.
      

      üìå 2024

      
        üìÑ On 1 July, two new companies are formally
        registered: Tributum AB (Org.nr: 559488-5484) and
        Aspiratio Holding AB (Org.nr: 559488-5476). Two new
        entities, pulled once again from the ever-stocked shelves of
        Bolagsstiftarna AB, specialists in shelf-company logistics.
      

      
        ‚öôÔ∏è Both entities are born with identical governance templates:
        temporary board members linked to G√∂teborg, all replaced within weeks.
        On 29 July, Sahar El Nasser and Daniella Dahl take
        formal control of both boards.
      

      
        üß± Tributum AB is declared as a restaurant business,
        while Aspiratio is set up as a property and asset
        manager. This distinction suggests an early intent to separate
        operational activities from holding structures.
      

      
        üìç Both are registered at the same address as HSSC and KEHDA, further
        reinforcing the emerging architecture. Whether these entities were
        created to absorb risk, optimize flows, or serve future roles remains to
        be clarified.
      
      
        Quan operates physically within the premises of Elite Hotel Esplanade,
        at M√§ster Johansgatan 15 in Malm√∂. While customers often believe they
        are dealing directly with hotel staff,
        <strong
          >the restaurant is managed independently, under separate legal
          entities</strong
        >.
      

      
        A quick search in the Swedish business register confirmed that
        HSSC Event AB was the legal entity linked to the
        restaurant. It listed Sahar El Nasser as
        suppleant (alternate board member), with no other listed
        responsibilities at that time.
      

      
        On public business directories such as Allabolag, the
        structure of HSSC Event AB appears minimal. The company is
        registered at the same address as Quan Restaurant, yet no explicit
        reference to the restaurant is made.
      

      
        Only two names are listed:
        Alexander Saahil Chudasama (ledamot) and
        Sahar El Nasser (suppleant). No shareholder information
        or operational description is available beyond this bare minimum.
      

      
        Meanwhile, Chudasama Invest AB, held by Alexander
        Chudasama, owns under 25% of shares. However, the 2021 Articles of
        Association grant him rights to appoint and dismiss the majority of the
        board, giving him de facto operational control.
      

      
        Lin Daniella Dahl and
        Henrik Kei Siebert are both registered at the same
        residential address in Trelleborg. Their shared domicile suggests a
        likely domestic relationship, although not formally stated in company
        documents.
      

      
        Sahar El Nasser and
        Alexander Saahil Chudasama also appear as cohabitants
        in Malm√∂, based on population registry data. This co-residency
        reinforces the possibility of internal alignment in the governance of
        HSSC Event AB.
      

      
        Though visibly committed during those shifts, his involvement remained
        minimal outside of them. He stayed socially distant, rarely interacting
        with staff or showing signs of operational leadership.
      
      
        What stood out to me was the
        <strong
          >complete absence of communication between Henrik and Sahar</strong
        >. During my three weeks at Quan, I never saw them speak or exchange
        even a glance. For someone trying to understand their role, this silence
        was striking.
      

      
        On July 1st, 2024, two new legal entities were
        incorporated on the same day: Tributum AB and
        Aspiratio Holding AB. Both companies list board members
        directly connected to Quan and share the exact same address:
        M√§ster Johansgatan 15, Malm√∂ ‚Äî the known location of Quan, HSSC
        Event AB, and Elite Hotel.
      

      
        By contrast, Aspiratio Holding AB is formally
        registered under c/o Kehda Holding AB, but still at the same
        Malm√∂ address. Despite being legally active, Aspiratio shows
        no declared business activity,
        no F-tax registration, no VAT (Moms),
        and no employer contributions.
      

      
        Its board lists Lin Daniella Dahl as chair and
        Sahar El Nasser as deputy ‚Äî forming the same tandem
        involved in Tributum, with overlapping but formally distinct roles. Both
        entities were created simultaneously and appear dormant or inactive on
        paper.
      

      
        No public record directly links Elite Hotels and
        HSSC Event AB. However, both companies officially
        operate from the same address:
        M√§ster Johansgatan 15, Malm√∂. This overlap may indicate
        a tenancy or subcontracting arrangement, but the absence of published
        contracts prevents confirmation.

        max-width: 740px;

    >
      Glossary


      
        Disclaimer
        
          A disclaimer is a legal statement that limits or
          denies liability for the consequences of using or interpreting
          published content.
        
        
          It is commonly placed at the end of web pages or documents, and
          clarifies that the information provided does not constitute legal or
          professional advice.
        
        
          Example on this site: ‚ÄúContent provided 'as is' without
          warranties. Terms governed by Swedish law ‚Äî Malm√∂ courts have
          exclusive jurisdiction.‚Äù
        
      
      
        Holding Company
        
          A Holding Company is an entity created to own shares
          in one or more other companies, usually without direct commercial
          operations of its own. Its purpose is to control, consolidate, or
          protect underlying business assets.
        
        
          In large corporate groups, a holding might coordinate finance, legal
          strategy, and investment flows across subsidiaries.
          In smaller setups or offshore structures, however, holdings may
          serve more symbolic or strategic purposes ‚Äî such as
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >isolating liabilities, fragmenting control, or hiding the true
            beneficial owner</span
          >.
        
        
          The term ‚Äúholding‚Äù does not guarantee operational depth.
          In your case, MedFood Holdings Ltd is registered in
          Cyprus, has no known employees or infrastructure, and serves
          exclusively as the legal owner of IzakayaKoi AB post-2004. This is a
          classic example of a passive holding vehicle ‚Äî potentially
          designed for tax or opacity purposes.
        
        
          A holding may appear legitimate in public records, yet be disconnected
          from the daily operations, which remain handled by nominees or
          external managers. That‚Äôs why
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >the title ‚Äúholding‚Äù must always be cross-examined</span
          >
          with actual business substance.
        
        
          In forensic work, holdings act as anchors: they centralize formal
          control but may not reflect the real ecosystem of people, payments,
          and power.
        
        
          In corporate genealogy, holdings are structural pivots</strong
          >: they signal transitions, ownership shifts, or hidden
          consolidations. Identifying their connections helps reconstruct
          ownership trees and expose coordination across legal entities.
        
     
      
        Legal Notice
        
          A legal notice (or mentions l√©gales in
          French) refers to the mandatory publication of identifying details
          about the entity behind a website, such as the publisher, address, VAT
          number, or legal operator.
        
        
          In Sweden, this is enforced under the
          E-commerce Act (2002:562) and ensures transparency,
          consumer protection, and traceability.
        
        
          Non-compliance can hinder legal recourse in disputes or complaints.
        
      
      
        Corporate Genealogy
        
          Corporate Genealogy is a method used to trace the ancestry and evolution of a business ‚Äî not just its current ownership, but its historical relationships, transitions, and patterns of influence.
        
        
          It examines how companies split, merge, rename, relocate, or rebrand, and how founders, family members, or key advisors continue to shape operations across decades, even without formal control.
        
        
          Unlike traditional ownership tracing (focused on shares), corporate genealogy includes:
          
            Shared addresses and staff over time
            Repeated use of certain lawyers, auditors, or advisors
            Legacy business models that reappear under new brands
            Succession of influence: who mentored or empowered whom
          
        
        
          Corporate genealogy is particularly useful when:
          
            Founders use multiple companies to test or launch variations
            Family control is passed on informally
            New entities are created to sidestep reputation or financial baggage
          
        
        
          It draws from archival research, forensic analysis, and pattern recognition. It's often used by investigative journalists, compliance lawyers, or private intelligence analysts to uncover long-term continuity disguised by legal fragmentation.
        
        
          üìå It helps answer: ‚ÄúWhere did this concept really come from?‚Äù or ‚ÄúWhy does this structure look familiar?‚Äù ‚Äî and allows us to understand why some actors never appear on paper, yet their influence is unmistakable.
        
      
      
        Forensic History
        
          Forensic History is the structured reconstruction of
          past events, decisions, and connections in order to understand how a
          situation unfolded ‚Äî especially in the context of conflict, risk, or
          hidden agendas.
        
        
          Unlike classic historical narrative, forensic history focuses on
          <strong
            >intentional omissions, grey zones, and invisible
            relationships</strong
          >. It aims to reassemble what was disaggregated ‚Äî legally,
          structurally, or rhetorically.
        
        
          It is particularly useful when
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >official documents appear clean</span
          >
          but a deeper logic of obfuscation or control is suspected. It
          mobilizes documents, registries, press archives, leaks, and timeline
          inconsistencies to create a coherent map.
        
        
          In your use case, forensic history helps determine
          when real ownership diverged from legal representation, and
          whether events (e.g. liquidation, resignations, trust formations) are
          symptoms of deeper coordination.
        
        
          Forensic history is used by investigative journalists, judicial
          commissions, corporate analysts, and researchers dealing with opaque
          ecosystems. It often reveals
          the intentional engineering of forgetting.
        
        
          It does not prove fraud directly ‚Äî but it builds a high-resolution
          narrative capable of exposing contradictions that justify deeper
          scrutiny.
        
      
      
        Four Corners Rule
        
          The Four Corners Rule is a legal principle stating
          that a document must be interpreted solely based on what is written
          ‚Äúwithin its four corners‚Äù ‚Äî meaning the four sides of the paper. No
          external evidence may be introduced to modify or explain the text
          unless the document is ambiguous.
        
        
          Originating in Anglo-American contract law, the
          doctrine is used in courts to determine the intent of a contract or
          agreement, by restricting analysis to its internal content.
          <u
            >Everything needed for interpretation must be found in the document
            itself</u
          >.
        
        
          In forensic work, this principle becomes relevant when documents (like
          shareholder agreements, minutes, audits) are drafted to appear
          self-contained and unambiguous ‚Äî even when their real function may be
          to disguise a transfer, an omission, or a hidden beneficiary.
        
        
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >The Four Corners Rule is useful to expose what is intentionally
            omitted</span
          >. When a document is silent on a topic that would logically be
          mentioned, the absence itself can become a clue ‚Äî especially when
          compared across versions or years.
        
        
          In your case, the principle helps evaluate whether documents (e.g.
          annual reports, resolutions, agreements) are ‚Äúcomplete‚Äù or were
          drafted to
          <strong
            >appear formally correct while omitting material relationships or
            changes of control</strong
          >.
        
        
          It is not a forensic tool in itself ‚Äî but it sets the ground for
          spotting legal engineering or documentary stagecraft, especially when
          paired with timeline analysis and external evidence.
        
      
      
        Principle of the 4 Coherences
        
          This method tests the plausibility of a structural or operational link
          between two entities by evaluating consistency across four forensic
          axes:
        
        
          
            Temporal Coherence: Do major events (e.g. share
            transfers, liquidations, restructurings) occur in synchrony or
            sequence?
          
          
            Geographic Coherence: Do both companies operate
            from the same physical or legal address? Any overlap in site usage
            or postal registrations?
          
          
            Financial Coherence: Are there interlinked cash
            flows (e.g. rent, loans, management fees)? Do declared profits and
            losses evolve in tandem or offset each other?
          
          
            Decision-Making Coherence: Do the same individuals
            appear in both boards, signatures, or meeting minutes?
          
        
        
          A strong match across all four dimensions can justify a hypothesis of
          concealed continuity, de facto control, or orchestrated restructuring
          ‚Äî even without a formal merger or holding structure.
        
      
      
        Theory A ‚Äì Risk-Sharing Structure
        
          This hypothesis assumes that multiple companies are maintained in
          parallel in order to distribute tax exposure or legal liability. One
          company (e.g. IzakayaKoi) takes on aggressive practices (undeclared
          cash, off-book transactions), while another (e.g. Steakhouse AB)
          remains ‚Äúclean‚Äù and operational.
        
        
          The goal is to let one entity absorb the risk ‚Äî tax audits, sanctions,
          or permanent revocation ‚Äî while keeping another entity
          <strong
            >shielded from scrutiny and ready to continue operations</strong
          >.
        
        
          This structure is most effective when
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >the clean company is superficially unconnected</span
          >
          but shares key characteristics: location, people, suppliers, and cash
          patterns.
        
        
          It often appears as a legal relay, where one entity ‚Äúfalls‚Äù while
          another quietly takes over without interruption.
        
      
      
        Theory B ‚Äì Asset Stripping Strategy
        
          This theory posits that one company is progressively emptied of its
          valuable assets (equipment, personnel, clientele, brand, cash) in
          favor of another ‚Äî typically a newer, safer, or less exposed entity.
        
        
          The original entity (e.g. IzakayaKoi AB) appears to decline in
          performance, while the receiving entity (e.g. Steakhouse AB) suddenly
          improves, often without a formal transfer or acquisition.
        
        
          Red flags include: underpriced asset sales,
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >overlapping employees or leases</span
          >, and strategic underreporting of profits in the stripped entity.
        
        
          The intent is to allow one company to "die" formally while another
          captures the value ‚Äî often in anticipation of bankruptcy, audit, or
          tax exposure.
        
      
      
        Board Member
        
          A Board Member is a legally registered director
          responsible for overseeing and formally representing the company‚Äôs
          interests. In most jurisdictions, this position grants voting power on
          key governance issues such as financial reporting, strategic
          decisions, and executive appointments.
        
        
          Board Members are usually appointed by shareholders. In larger
          companies, they are selected for their experience or expertise and may
          sit as part of a multi-member board with clear role distributions
          (Chairperson, Treasurer, etc.).
          <strong
            >In smaller companies, the board may consist of a single
            individual</strong
          >
          ‚Äî often the founder or a family member ‚Äî making the board structure a
          legal formality rather than a functioning body.
        
        
          The presence of only one board member (especially
          when coupled with a Deputy Board Member but no wider
          governance team) often reflects a tightly held company,
          possibly a shell entity, or a low-activity business.
          In forensic terms, this may suggest risk exposure due to limited
          oversight or consolidated control.
        
        
          Board members have personal legal liability in cases
          of fraudulent reporting, tax evasion, or corporate negligence. Their
          names are typically listed in national company registries and can be
          tracked across multiple entities to detect patterns of control,
          influence, or recurring irregularities.
        
        
          The board structure serves
          both functional and symbolic purposes. In robust
          firms, it supports governance and transparency. In minimal structures,
          it may serve only to meet registration requirements while
          shielding decision-makers behind formal titles.
        
        
          In corporate genealogy, board members are essential markers for
          tracing continuity and control across legal entities, especially when
          company names or registration numbers change but human operators
          remain the same.
        
      
      
        Deputy Board Member
        
          A Deputy Board Member (or
          Alternate Director) is a legally designated substitute who
          takes over a Board Member‚Äôs duties
          <strong
            >in case of death, resignation, illness, or formal absence</strong
          >. Outside of such events, this role is passive and has no legal
          authority or voting power.
        
        
          In smaller companies or single-director firms, this
          role is often added for compliance reasons.
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >Swedish law, for example, requires the nomination of a deputy if
            the board has only one formal member</span
          >. The deputy ensures administrative continuity without implying any
          real involvement.
        
        
          This position is typically symbolic and rarely
          activated in practice. In many cases, deputy members are friends,
          family members, or legal acquaintances of the main director ‚Äî not
          selected for oversight capacity but simply to satisfy registry
          conditions.
        
        
          From a forensic standpoint, the appointment of a
          <strong
            >Deputy Board Member with no corporate activity or public
            presence</strong
          >
          can be an indicator of a closed governance model. It may also suggest
          that the formal board is not the true locus of power, especially when
          the same names appear repeatedly across related legal entities.
        
        
          While technically part of the governance framework,
          <strong
            >the deputy board member holds no operational role unless
            activated</strong
          >. This makes it difficult to assess their knowledge of day-to-day
          operations or accountability in irregular situations.
        
        
          In corporate genealogy, deputy members are worth noting primarily to
          reveal structural minimalism or strategic patterns ‚Äî such as legal
          insulation of the primary board member through dormant or nominal
          substitutes.
        
      
      
        Auditor
        
          An Auditor (or statutory auditor) is an
          external party legally appointed to review, verify, and sign
          off on a company‚Äôs financial statements. Their mission is to certify
          that the accounts give a fair view of the company's financial position
          and comply with applicable laws.
        
        
          In larger corporations, this role is held by licensed
          audit firms (e.g., KPMG, PwC) and plays a crucial part in investor
          confidence and regulatory compliance.
          In small private companies, the auditor is often an independent
          accountant ‚Äî or sometimes a close associate ‚Äî with a role that is
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >more formal than substantial</span
          >.
        
        
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >Auditors must be independent</span
          >, both in function and appearance. They are legally barred from
          management roles or shareholding. However, in practice ‚Äî
          especially in small firms ‚Äî the auditor may be a friend, former
          consultant, or recurring figure validating multiple companies across a
          network.
        
        
          The identity of the auditor is often a critical
          forensic clue: do they appear in other linked firms? Are they involved
          in known tax audits? A passive or unqualified auditor may
          indicate systemic opacity or administrative negligence.
        
        
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >This role is a legal residue</span
          >
          from 20th-century commercial codes, where trust between stakeholders
          required third-party oversight.
          <u
            >Today, audit requirements are often waived below certain
            thresholds</u
          >, yet many companies keep the title for compliance or image purposes
          ‚Äî even if the audit is superficial.
        
        
          In forensic history and corporate genealogy, the auditor may not hold
          power, but
          their recurrence across entities is a red flag. They
          help identify hidden connections, legal insulation tactics, or serial
          patterns of governance without transparency.
        
      
      
        Deputy Auditor
        
          A Deputy Auditor (or alternate auditor) is a
          legal substitute for the main auditor, stepping in only if the primary
          auditor resigns, becomes incapacitated, or is otherwise unable to
          fulfill their role. Outside of such circumstances, the deputy
          has no official function, no signature power, and no influence on the
          company's financial reporting.
        
        
          In many jurisdictions ‚Äî including Sweden ‚Äî
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >this position is a formal safeguard</span
          >, required only when an official auditor is appointed. The deputy
          exists to preserve continuity in the audit process, but
          in practice, is rarely involved unless triggered by an
          unforeseen event.
        
        
          In small or private companies, deputy auditors are
          often individuals with no active link to the business: acquaintances,
          family members, or professionals added to satisfy registration forms.
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >Their appointment does not indicate active oversight</span
          >, and they typically do not participate in meetings or review
          internal documents.
        
        
          From a forensic perspective,
          <strong
            >deputy auditors may help confirm structural minimalism</strong
          >
          ‚Äî especially when their names never appear elsewhere in the corporate
          ecosystem. If they reappear across related entities, however, it may
          suggest the existence of a revolving governance shell or shadow
          network.
        
        
          <u
            >Deputy auditors are not bound by the same intensity of reporting
            obligations as main auditors</u
          >, yet they still carry a degree of formal responsibility if
          activated. This duality ‚Äî formal but dormant ‚Äî makes them useful
          markers for identifying when a company is built more for legal
          compliance than operational robustness.
        
        
          In genealogy work, deputy auditors are
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >low-signal but high-value datapoints</span
          >: they rarely act, but their mere presence reflects how a company
          anticipates legal risk. Their invisibility in practice is often the
          very sign of a shallow governance layer.
        
      
      
        Offshore Country
        
          An Offshore Country refers to a jurisdiction where
          companies can be registered with minimal regulatory requirements, low
          or zero corporate taxes, and often strong confidentiality laws. These
          jurisdictions are sometimes used to create legal distance between
          ownership and operation.
        
        
          Examples include Cyprus, Panama, and Costa Rica. Companies
          registered there may act as passive owners of other entities abroad,
          while concealing the identity of the true controlling party.
        
        
          These legal structures often allow nominee directors or legal
          representatives to appear on official documents, while
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >the beneficial owner remains hidden</span
          >
          through trusts or corporate layers.
        
        
          Offshore does not mean illegal, but these countries are often
          found in investigations involving complex asset transfers, tax
          structuring, or shell companies with no visible operations.
        
        
          In forensic work,
          offshore jurisdictions function as blind spots ‚Äî
          deliberately or not ‚Äî breaking traceability between control and
          accountability unless other documents (financial statements, leaks, or
          court filings) allow connections to be restored.
        
        
          In corporate genealogy, they often mark transitions in ownership
          strategy, opacity level, or jurisdictional anchoring, especially in
          periods of restructuring or risk exposure.
        
      
      
        Holding Company
        
          A Holding Company is a legal entity created to own
          shares in one or more other companies. It typically does not produce
          goods or services itself but exists to manage equity, coordinate
          ownership, or consolidate financial control.
        
        
          In large corporate groups, holding companies may centralize
          strategy, tax optimization, or risk management across subsidiaries.
          However,
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >in smaller or offshore structures</span
          >, they may have little or no operational activity and serve more as
          legal containers.
        
        
          <strong
            >The word ‚Äúholding‚Äù does not guarantee operational depth</strong
          >. Some entities with this label are dormant, symbolic, or registered
          in secrecy jurisdictions. Their purpose can include
          insulating liabilities, obscuring control chains, or
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >fragmenting ownership visibility</span
          >.
        
        
          Holding companies are often used to group together several businesses
          under a common ownership umbrella, but they can also appear in
          multi-layered ownership networks where the real actors remain behind
          nominees or corporate veils.
        
        
          In forensic analysis, a holding company may act as an anchor ‚Äî it
          holds the legal link to assets, but not necessarily the power to
          operate or decide. Identifying who controls the holding itself is
          often more important than the holding‚Äôs official status.
        
        
          In corporate genealogy,
          holdings mark key transitions: acquisitions,
          consolidations, spin-offs, or restructurings. They are critical nodes
          for tracing continuity and control through complex ownership chains.
        
      
      
        PPOWER(E) Method

        
          The PPOWER(E) method is a simple tool to figure out who really
          controls a business ‚Äî not just on paper, but in practice. It‚Äôs used
          when official ownership doesn‚Äôt match what‚Äôs actually happening on the
          ground.
        

        
          The name stands for six key things to check. If one person or group
          shows up on most of them, they‚Äôre likely in charge ‚Äî even if they
          don‚Äôt legally ‚Äúown‚Äù anything.
        

        <table
          style="width: 100%; border-collapse: collapse; font-size: 0.95em"
        >
          
            
              Axis
              What to look for
            
          
          
            
              P ‚Äì Power
              
                Who gives orders? Who takes the real decisions?
              
            
            
              P ‚Äì Property
              
                Who owns it ‚Äî even indirectly or through someone else?
              
            
            
              O ‚Äì Operation
              
                Who runs it day to day? Who shows up on site?
              
            
            
              W ‚Äì Wallet
              
                Who receives payments? Who pays the bills?
              
            
            
              E ‚Äì Employees
              
                Are staff shared across companies? Who hires them?
              
            
            
              R ‚Äì Reputation
              
                Who is publicly seen as ‚Äúthe boss‚Äù or the face of the company?
              
            
          
        

        
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >In your case, this is useful to understand how HSSC, Aspircio,
            Queda Consulting and Tributum AB might be controlled by the same
            group ‚Äî without sharing official owners.</span
          >
        

        üìö Where does it come from?
        
          The method was first developed in the 2010s by financial investigators
          working on corruption and shell companies. It‚Äôs now used by
          investigative journalists, fraud examiners, and forensic analysts to
          spot real control hidden behind fake legal structures.
        
      
      
        Panama Papers
        
          The Panama Papers refer to a large-scale data leak
          published in 2016, exposing over 11.5 million confidential documents
          from the Panamanian law firm Mossack Fonseca. These files
          revealed the global use of offshore companies to conceal ownership,
          shift assets, or optimize taxation.
        
        
          The leak was obtained by a whistleblower and shared with the German
          newspaper S√ºddeutsche Zeitung, which partnered with the
          ICIJ (International Consortium of Investigative
          Journalists) to coordinate a worldwide investigation across more than
          80 countries.
        
        
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >The documents named over 200,000 offshore entities</span
          >, many linked to public figures, politicians, business magnates, and
          intermediaries in tax havens like Panama, the British Virgin Islands,
          Cyprus, and Seychelles.
        
        
          The Panama Papers do not prove illegality by themselves.
          However, they exposed structures often used to
          <strong
            >conceal beneficial ownership, avoid scrutiny, or simulate distance
            between control and responsibility</strong
          >.
        
        
          In forensic investigations, Panama Papers records are used to trace
          hidden corporate relationships, nominee directors,
          and cross-border control networks. The ICIJ provides a free searchable
          database of companies, agents, and addresses mentioned in the leak.
        
        
          In corporate genealogy, the Panama Papers serve as a historical
          milestone ‚Äî a public map of how formal company structures can be used
          to shape narratives of legitimacy while shielding complex financial
          arrangements.
        
      
      
        Forensic Accounting
        
          Forensic Accounting refers to the specialized
          analysis of financial records in order to detect, explain, or prove
          fraud, manipulation, or hidden transactions. It goes beyond standard
          auditing by focusing on intentional irregularities or deceptive
          practices.
        
        
          Practitioners combine accounting expertise with investigative
          techniques to reveal
          <u
            >where money has gone, who benefited, and whether numbers reflect
            real activity</u
          >. This often involves tracing the flow of funds, identifying
          fictitious invoices, undeclared revenues, or disguised expenses.
        
        
          In the context of small businesses or shell companies, forensic
          accounting is used to
          spot sudden profitability shifts,
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >abnormally timed dividends</span
          >, or implausible operating margins ‚Äî especially when these
          precede a liquidation, transfer of shares, or tax audit.
        
        
          The method is particularly useful when a company presents a legal
          appearance of normality but maintains internal inconsistencies between
          declared income and operational scale. It helps distinguish between
          genuine decline and strategic concealment.
        
        
          Forensic accounting is widely used in tax disputes, fraud litigation,
          bankruptcy proceedings, and corporate investigations ‚Äî both in courts
          and by journalists, regulators, or internal auditors.
        
        
          In your use case, forensic accounting underpins the detection of
          <span style="background-color: #e5e7eb"
            >profit inflation followed by asset extraction</span
          >, and helps anchor suspicion when no legal violation is yet
          officially stated.
        
      
        
          Liability Mapping
          
            Liability Mapping is the forensic analysis of who is legally, financially, or reputationally responsible for decisions made within a corporate structure ‚Äî especially when ownership, operations, and communication are spread across multiple legal entities.
          
          
            It is commonly used when the formal governance structure does not match the actual flow of authority or risk. In such cases, liability may not rest with the nominal board or shareholder, but with a hidden actor who drives operations, hires staff, or approves spending.
          
          
            Liability mapping seeks to answer questions like:
            
              Who can be held accountable if something goes wrong?
              Which entity is exposed to legal claims, and who signed the contracts?
              Can risk be ‚Äúdispersed‚Äù through proxies, layers, or dormant companies?
            
          
          
            This mapping is crucial in:
            
              Hybrid operations (where employees work across entities)
              Multi-tenant locations (like restaurants operating inside hotels)
              Family businesses using layers to reduce visibility or isolate debt
            
          
          
            It complements tools like PPOWER(E) by highlighting not just who controls, but who would be held accountable in court or press.
          
          
            ‚ö†Ô∏è In some cases, liability is purposely obfuscated through nominee directors, offshore intermediaries, or asset-free operating shells. Liability Mapping is the discipline that seeks to pierce this veil.
          
        
          
            Shadow Governance
            
              Shadow Governance refers to a structure of informal or hidden control within a company or organization, where real decisions are made by individuals who are not officially listed as board members, shareholders, or legal signatories.
            
            
              These actors may exert power through personal ties (family, spouses, long-time collaborators), financial leverage, or influence over day-to-day operations ‚Äî without leaving a legal trace in public records. They can shape budgets, hiring, strategy, or even ownership changes from the shadows.
            
            
              Shadow governance is often used to:
              
                Maintain control without legal responsibility or visibility
                Protect founders from liability or reputational risk
                Divide real power among informal groups (e.g., family councils, trusted proxies)
                Create plausible deniability in the event of legal scrutiny
              
            
            
              In practice, shadow governance is common in:
              
                Family businesses (where elders or relatives informally direct decisions)
                Founder-run groups with nominal boards or straw directors
                International or offshore structures where power is transferred via mandate, trust, or front companies
              
            
            
              Forensic analysts often detect shadow governance through indirect signals:
              
                Repeated presence of the same individuals across unrelated companies
                Discrepancy between operational authority and legal registration
                Changes made ‚Äúoff the books‚Äù or without documented board consent
              
            
            
              üìå Shadow governance does not always imply wrongdoing ‚Äî it can be the result of tradition, trust, or pragmatism. But in risk analysis, it represents a critical blind spot: where control is real, but responsibility is hidden.

            communications.

            called a
            <a

            >: the smallest recorded set of meaningful

            >

            About the Purpose of This Log
          

          
            Publishing these technical and editorial logs serves a clear and
            deliberate purpose. Beyond documenting the construction of the
            Aftershift blog, this public log is designed to proactively
            demonstrate discipline, transparency, and continuity throughout the
            development process.
          

          
            Although no law requires an individual to publish construction logs,
            this initiative is guided by important principles recognized in
            Swedish and European contexts:
          

          
            
              Good faith (God tro): Acting in a loyal, honest,
              and serious manner during disputes or work-related actions.
            
            
              Burden of proof (Bevisb√∂rda): Taking
              responsibility for proving one's claims when challenged.
            
            
              <strong
                >Best documentation practices (spirit of
                Dokumentationsskyldighet)</strong
              >: Ensuring traceability and integrity through verifiable records.
            
          

          
            Maintaining this public log also provides a defense against
            potential allegations that could arise in the context of employment
            disputes, such as:
          

          
            
              Bad faith ‚Äì Continuous documentation shows
              commitment and seriousness.
            
            
              Disorganization ‚Äì Structured updates demonstrate
              methodical work.
            
            
              Abandonment of efforts ‚Äì Regular updates confirm
              ongoing engagement.
            
            
              Improvisation or chaotic behavior ‚Äì Recorded
              evolution shows planning and consistency.
            
            
              Retroactive falsification ‚Äì Timestamped updates
              prevent any suspicion of post hoc fabrication.
            
          

          
            In Swedish legal practice, behavior is often judged not only on
            strict laws but also on the parties' credibility, rigor, and
            seriousness. By maintaining this verifiable log, Aftershift
            reinforces its credibility and integrity in a transparent,
            professional manner.

              responsibility for proving one's claims when challenged.
            
            
              <strong
                >Best documentation practices (spirit of
                Dokumentationsskyldighet)</strong
              >: Ensuring traceability and integrity through verifiable records.
            
          

          
            Maintaining this public log also provides a defense against
            potential allegations that could arise in the context of employment
            disputes, such as:
          

          
            
              Bad faith ‚Äì Continuous documentation shows
              commitment and seriousness.
            
            
              Disorganization ‚Äì Structured updates demonstrate
              methodical work.
            
            
              Abandonment of efforts ‚Äì Regular updates confirm
              ongoing engagement.
            
            
              Improvisation or chaotic behavior ‚Äì Recorded
              evolution shows planning and consistency.
            
            
              Retroactive falsification ‚Äì Timestamped updates
              prevent any suspicion of post hoc fabrication.
            
          

          
            In Swedish legal practice, behavior is often judged not only on
            strict laws but also on the parties' credibility, rigor, and
            seriousness. By maintaining this verifiable log, Aftershift
            reinforces its credibility and integrity in a transparent,
            professional manner.

  // Script pour la sidebar
  const toggleBtn = document.getElementById("toggleNavbar");
  const navbar = document.querySelector(".navbar");
  toggleBtn?.addEventListener("click", () => {
    navbar.classList.toggle("collapsed");
  });

  // Script pour injecter le footer
  fetch("/components/footer.html")
    .then(res => res.text())
    .then(html => {
      const footerContainer = document.createElement("div");
      footerContainer.innerHTML = html;
      document.body.appendChild(footerContainer);
    });

        Activity Log
        <small class="timestamp" style="display: block; text-align: center"
          >Last updated: Thursday, May 1, 2025 at 02:33 AM</small
        >

        
          About This Update Section
          
            This section documents the continuous technical and editorial
            adjustments made to the blog.
          
          
            In accordance with general principles of evidence and transparency,
            each update is timestamped to ensure the traceability and integrity
            of modifications over time.
          
          
            All timestamps recorded here correspond to the precise moment when
            the changes became effective and publicly visible online, in line
            with recognized standards of probative value in digital
            communications.
          
          
            In this section, each update corresponds to what is technically
            called a
            <a
              href="https://docs.github.com/en/get-started/quickstart/github-glossary#commit"
              target="_blank"
              >commit</a
            >: the smallest recorded set of meaningful
            <a
              href="https://docs.github.com/en/pull-requests/committing-changes-to-your-project/creating-and-editing-commits/about-commits"
              target="_blank"
              >modifications</a
            >
            saved within our version control system.
          
          
            Note: The line at the bottom summarizes yesterday‚Äôs total
            updates and the number of files affected, giving a clear,
            at-a-glance overview of daily activity without listing every change.
          
        
        
        
          
            About the Purpose of This Log
          

          
            Publishing these technical and editorial logs serves a clear and
            deliberate purpose. Beyond documenting the construction of the
            Aftershift blog, this public log is designed to proactively
            demonstrate discipline, transparency, and continuity throughout the
            development process.
          

          
            Although no law requires an individual to publish construction logs,
            this initiative is guided by important principles recognized in
            Swedish and European contexts:
          

          
            
              Good faith (God tro): Acting in a loyal, honest,
              and serious manner during disputes or work-related actions.
            
            
              Burden of proof (Bevisb√∂rda): Taking
              responsibility for proving one's claims when challenged.
            
            
              <strong
                >Best documentation practices (spirit of
                Dokumentationsskyldighet)</strong
              >: Ensuring traceability and integrity through verifiable records.
            
          

          
            Maintaining this public log also provides a defense against
            potential allegations that could arise in the context of employment
            disputes, such as:
          

          
            
              Bad faith ‚Äì Continuous documentation shows
              commitment and seriousness.
            
            
              Disorganization ‚Äì Structured updates demonstrate
              methodical work.
            
            
              Abandonment of efforts ‚Äì Regular updates confirm
              ongoing engagement.
            
            
              Improvisation or chaotic behavior ‚Äì Recorded
              evolution shows planning and consistency.
            
            
              Retroactive falsification ‚Äì Timestamped updates
              prevent any suspicion of post hoc fabrication.
            
          

          
            In Swedish legal practice, behavior is often judged not only on
            strict laws but also on the parties' credibility, rigor, and
            seriousness. By maintaining this verifiable log, Aftershift
            reinforces its credibility and integrity in a transparent,
            professional manner.

  // Script pour la sidebar
  const toggleBtn = document.getElementById("toggleNavbar");
  const navbar = document.querySelector(".navbar");
  toggleBtn?.addEventListener("click", () => {
    navbar.classList.toggle("collapsed");
  });

  // Script pour injecter le footer
  fetch("/components/footer.html")
    .then(res => res.text())
    .then(html => {
      const footerContainer = document.createElement("div");
      footerContainer.innerHTML = html;
      document.body.appendChild(footerContainer);
    });

      style="
        max-width: 740px;

        Activity Log
        <small class="timestamp" style="display: block; text-align: center"
          >Last updated: Thursday, May 1, 2025 at 02:33 AM</small
        >

        
          About This Update Section
          
            This section documents the continuous technical and editorial
            adjustments made to the blog.
          
          
            In accordance with general principles of evidence and transparency,
            each update is timestamped to ensure the traceability and integrity
            of modifications over time.
          
          
            All timestamps recorded here correspond to the precise moment when
            the changes became effective and publicly visible online, in line
            with recognized standards of probative value in digital
            communications.
          
          
            In this section, each update corresponds to what is technically
            called a
            <a
              href="https://docs.github.com/en/get-started/quickstart/github-glossary#commit"
              target="_blank"
              >commit</a
            >: the smallest recorded set of meaningful
            <a
              href="https://docs.github.com/en/pull-requests/committing-changes-to-your-project/creating-and-editing-commits/about-commits"
              target="_blank"
              >modifications</a
            >
            saved within our version control system.
          
          
            Note: The line at the bottom summarizes yesterday‚Äôs total
            updates and the number of files affected, giving a clear,
            at-a-glance overview of daily activity without listing every change.
          
        
        
        
          
            About the Purpose of This Log
          

          
            Publishing these technical and editorial logs serves a clear and
            deliberate purpose. Beyond documenting the construction of the
            Aftershift blog, this public log is designed to proactively
            demonstrate discipline, transparency, and continuity throughout the
            development process.
          

          
            Although no law requires an individual to publish construction logs,
            this initiative is guided by important principles recognized in
            Swedish and European contexts:
          

          
            
              Good faith (God tro): Acting in a loyal, honest,
              and serious manner during disputes or work-related actions.
            
            
              Burden of proof (Bevisb√∂rda): Taking
              responsibility for proving one's claims when challenged.
            
            
              <strong
                >Best documentation practices (spirit of
                Dokumentationsskyldighet)</strong
              >: Ensuring traceability and integrity through verifiable records.
            
          

          
            Maintaining this public log also provides a defense against
            potential allegations that could arise in the context of employment
            disputes, such as:
          

          
            
              Bad faith ‚Äì Continuous documentation shows
              commitment and seriousness.
            
            
              Disorganization ‚Äì Structured updates demonstrate
              methodical work.
            
            
              Abandonment of efforts ‚Äì Regular updates confirm
              ongoing engagement.
            
            
              Improvisation or chaotic behavior ‚Äì Recorded
              evolution shows planning and consistency.
            
            
              Retroactive falsification ‚Äì Timestamped updates
              prevent any suspicion of post hoc fabrication.
            
          

          
            In Swedish legal practice, behavior is often judged not only on
            strict laws but also on the parties' credibility, rigor, and
            seriousness. By maintaining this verifiable log, Aftershift
            reinforces its credibility and integrity in a transparent,
            professional manner.

              responsibility for proving one's claims when challenged.
            
            
              <strong
                >Best documentation practices (spirit of
                Dokumentationsskyldighet)</strong
              >: Ensuring traceability and integrity through verifiable records.
            
          

          
            Maintaining this public log also provides a defense against
            potential allegations that could arise in the context of employment
            disputes, such as:
          

          
            
              Bad faith ‚Äì Continuous documentation shows
              commitment and seriousness.
            
            
              Disorganization ‚Äì Structured updates demonstrate
              methodical work.
            
            
              Abandonment of efforts ‚Äì Regular updates confirm
              ongoing engagement.
            
            
              Improvisation or chaotic behavior ‚Äì Recorded
              evolution shows planning and consistency.
            
            
              Retroactive falsification ‚Äì Timestamped updates
              prevent any suspicion of post hoc fabrication.
            
          

          
            In Swedish legal practice, behavior is often judged not only on
            strict laws but also on the parties' credibility, rigor, and
            seriousness. By maintaining this verifiable log, Aftershift
            reinforces its credibility and integrity in a transparent,
            professional manner.

  // Script pour la sidebar
  const toggleBtn = document.getElementById("toggleNavbar");
  const navbar = document.querySelector(".navbar");
  toggleBtn?.addEventListener("click", () => {
    navbar.classList.toggle("collapsed");
  });

  // Script pour injecter le footer
  fetch("/components/footer.html")
    .then(res => res.text())
    .then(html => {
      const footerContainer = document.createElement("div");
      footerContainer.innerHTML = html;
      document.body.appendChild(footerContainer);
    });
